Third attack: turning-boundary asymptotics.

At a generic turning boundary M=0, M′≠0, N≠0M=0, M′=0, N=0, the primal graph in (μ,λ)(μ,λ) has a vertical tangent. If (μb,λb)(μb​,λb​) is the boundary point, then the dual curve has asymptote

μ−μb​=a(λ−λb​)2+⋯.

So the sign of the first deviation from the asymptote is controlled by aa, equivalently by the second λλ-derivative of μμ at the turning point. This is what makes adjacent dual arcs approach the common asymptote from opposite sides.

That is exactly enough for the local adjacent turning theorem, but it still does not globalize. It only tells you how each dual arc leaves its own turning-boundary asymptote. It does not stop a later nonadjacent same-parity arc from returning to the same vertical line in the dual plane.

Yes. Here is the cleanest math-form summary of what we have learned since the old “zero-capture is the main target” state, written from the standpoint of our running brainstorm, not the older draft framing.
1. The proof architecture has changed

The main structural change is that the geometry is no longer “one generic adjacent-boundary theorem plus convexity.” It has split into three distinct layers:

    the direct septic / order-7 algebra for the canonical second residual Δ7Δ7​;

    the local geometry of the normalized curve at W=0, M≠0W=0, M=0 boundaries;

    the global determinant / line-incidence problem for

D(s,t,u):=det⁡(F(s),F(t),F(u)),F=(c,v5,Δ7).
D(s,t,u):=det(F(s),F(t),F(u)),F=(c,v5​,Δ7​).

So the old bottleneck was too coarse: we are no longer simply “stuck on zero-capture.” We have a much sharper decomposition of what is local, what is global, and what still depends on the order-7 package.
2. The direct order-7 slice is real, canonical at the highest-new level, and not a fake witness

The direct q(7)q(7)-driven septic K1K1​-transport slice has been isolated and shown to be II-directional:
v7,K1(q(7))=0,u7,K1(q(7))=κ((x2−x1)ν6(q(7))+v(γ5−α5)(q(7))),
v7,K1​(q(7))​=0,u7,K1​(q(7))​=κ((x2​−x1​)ν6(q(7))​+v(γ5​−α5​)(q(7))),

so
Δ7(q(7))=u7(q(7))v5.
Δ7(q(7))​=u7(q(7))​v5​.

Moreover, the parity/weight-one reduction shows that the highest genuinely new q(7)q(7)-coefficient of Δ7Δ7​ comes only from the direct K1K1​ slice:
[Δ7][1]=[Δ7,K1][1].
[Δ7​][1]=[Δ7,K1​​][1].

So at the highest-new level, the Δ7Δ7​-geometry is already decided at order 77, not by some new primitive order-99 invariant.
3. The highest-new coefficient has been explicitly identified and is generically nonzero

In the minimal graded model, the direct highest-new coefficient is explicitly
(x2−x1)ν6(q(7))+v(γ5−α5)(q(7))=eu (a2+ab−b2)a2b4(a+b)2,
(x2​−x1​)ν6(q(7))​+v(γ5​−α5​)(q(7))=a2b4(a+b)2eu(a2+ab−b2)​,

so generically it is nonzero. Equivalently, the highest-new scalar
λ7:=[Δ7][1]
λ7​:=[Δ7​][1]

is already explicitly controlled by the direct septic K1K1​-slice and is generically nontrivial. This kills the easy “maybe the order-7 witness cancels out” possibility.
4. But the easy sign miracle failed

Although the direct highest-new coefficient is explicit, it is not sign-definite in the generic graded model, because the factor
a2+ab−b2
a2+ab−b2

changes sign as b/ab/a crosses (1+5)/2(1+5
​)/2, and the overall sign also depends on eueu. So the highest-new scalar is explicit enough to prove survival / noncancellation, but not explicit enough to force a trivial one-sided sign theorem. In particular, the easiest possible route “prove ϕϕ has one sign and finish” is gone.
5. The W=0, M≠0W=0, M=0 side is no longer the broad generic obstruction it once looked like

At a boundary with
c(hb)≠0,M(hb)≠0,W(hb)=0,
c(hb​)=0,M(hb​)=0,W(hb​)=0,

the normalized affine chart
x=v5c,y=Δ7c
x=cv5​​,y=cΔ7​​

has
d2ydx2=c3WM3,
dx2d2y​=M3c3W​,

so W=0, M≠0W=0, M=0 is exactly the affine-inflection regime. The generic local model is an ordinary odd-order inflection, with the cubic coefficient controlled by W′(hb)W′(hb​) in the simple case. This means the old adjacent tangent-separator route genuinely fails there; the local model is not “tangent-separator sign regularity with a missing proof,” it is an affine inflection where that statement is false.
6. Finite-order W=0, M≠0W=0, M=0 boundaries are locally sterile for pair-pair birth

This is one of the biggest actual theorems we gained. If WW has finite vanishing order rr at a boundary with M≠0M=0, then in the local affine coordinate x=v5/cx=v5​/c one gets
f′′(x)∼λxr,
f′′(x)∼λxr,

and the three-point determinant factors through the second divided difference. The resulting local theorem is:

    if rr is even, then for fixed same-side pair s<ts<t, the opposite-side determinant equation has no nearby zero;

    if rr is odd, it has at most one nearby opposite-side zero.

So no finite-order boundary of type W=0, M≠0W=0, M=0 can support a local pair-pair birth. This is stronger than the original “simple W=0W=0” story; it shows that every finite-order sign-changing inflection boundary is locally pair-pair sterile.
7. Open-interval W≡0W≡0 flatness on an M≠0M=0 region is excluded

Using the projective-Wronskian bridge,
(NM)′=0⟹Δ7c=Av5c+B⟹Δ7=A v5+B c,
(MN​)′=0⟹cΔ7​​=Acv5​​+B⟹Δ7​=Av5​+Bc,

and this affine dependence contradicts the non-affinity theorem for Δ7/cΔ7​/c under the direct septic nonvanishing hypothesis. So on any connected open interval with
c≠0,M≠0,
c=0,M=0,

one has
W≢0.
W≡0.

This means the W=0, M≠0W=0, M=0 side is not threatened by open-interval flatness; the only remaining local issue there is isolated behavior, and finite-order isolated points are already locally sterile.
8. The turning-boundary side has also improved: actual adjacent pair-pair exclusion is now unconditional

For generic turning boundaries
M(hb)=0,M′(hb)≠0,N(hb)≠0,
M(hb​)=0,M′(hb​)=0,N(hb​)=0,

we no longer only have the older conditional tangent-separator / zero-capture route. The brainstorm found a stronger local closure:

    strip exclusion against a compact opposite branch;

    compact first-contact;

    first-contact ⇒⇒ tangency;

    contradiction by adjacent slope-range separation.

This yields an unconditional theorem: no finite-slope line can be 22-secant to both adjacent branches across a generic turning boundary. The older stronger symmetric directional-kernel theorem still exists conditionally on symmetric zero-capture, but for actual adjacent pair-pair configurations, the local turning-boundary geometry is now closed without needing full zero-capture.
9. So the local story is now: both generic boundary types are locally benign

After all these attacks, the local picture is now:

    W=0, M≠0W=0, M=0: finite-order points are locally pair-pair sterile;

    generic turning boundaries: adjacent pair-pair is unconditionally excluded.

So the remaining global obstruction is not local birth of bad 2+22+2 lines at either generic boundary type. That is a major conceptual change from the old “zero-capture is the main target” state.
10. The determinant route is real: there is an exact mean-value / Peano-kernel theorem

We also learned that the determinant route is not just a slogan. The normalized determinant
Q(s,t,u):=D(s,t,u)(t−s)(u−s)(u−t)
Q(s,t,u):=(t−s)(u−s)(u−t)D(s,t,u)​

really is a generalized second divided difference. In particular, there is an exact mean-value / Peano-kernel representation, and on any interval where WW has fixed nonzero sign, this yields discrete sign-regularity of order 33 for the triple (c,v5,Δ7)(c,v5​,Δ7​). In plain terms: on a fixed-sign WW-interval, ordered triples have the right determinant sign and no three points are collinear. This is stronger than the original infinitesimal ECT viewpoint.
11. But the naive global “positive kernel / variation diminishing” route failed

The exact Peano-kernel formula also showed the limitation: once you rewrite
Q(u)=Q(s,t,u)
Q(u)=Q(s,t,u)

as a positive-kernel transform of WW, the corresponding scalar ODE reformulation
R′′=W
R′′=W

does not by itself force one-way sign transport. A concrete scalar counterexample shows the sign of Q(u)Q(u) can disappear and then reappear. So positivity of the kernel alone is not enough to globalize the no-four-secant theorem. This killed one of the most attractive generic routes.
12. The right projective coordinates are (μ,λ)(μ,λ), not (ρ1,ρ2)(ρ1​,ρ2​)

A major conceptual gain was the (μ,λ)(μ,λ)-reduction:
μ=cv5,λ=Δ7v5.
μ=v5​c​,λ=v5​Δ7​​.

In these coordinates, a line in the old chart becomes an ordinary affine line
λ=bμ+m,
λ=bμ+m,

and WW becomes exact graph curvature:

dμ2d2λ​=M3v53​​W.

So:

    W=0W=0 means λλ is affine in μμ;

    WW-sign intervals are ordinary convex/concave graph pieces;

    finite-order W=0W=0 are ordinary inflections of that graph.

This is the cleanest local geometric reformulation we found.
13. The true scalar slope variable is β=−L/Mβ=−L/M

Define
L:=v5Δ7′−Δ7v5′.
L:=v5​Δ7′​−Δ7​v5′​.

Then the tangent slope of the (μ,λ)(μ,λ)-graph is

β:=dμdλ​=−ML​,

and it satisfies the exact scalar evolution law
β′=−v5M2W.
β′=−M2v5​​W.

So the entire global tangent-slope recurrence problem has been reduced to the level-set recurrence problem for one scalar function β(h)β(h). This is one of the sharpest reductions we found.
14. The dual tangent-line curve is exact and highly structured

If
T(h):=(b(h),m(h))=(−L(h)M(h),N(h)M(h)),
T(h):=(b(h),m(h))=(−M(h)L(h)​,M(h)N(h)​),

then T(h)T(h) is the tangent-line curve in the dual (b,m)(b,m)-plane. It satisfies the exact differential identities
T′(h)=W(h)M(h)2 (−v5(h),c(h)),
T′(h)=M(h)2W(h)​(−v5​(h),c(h)),

and
det⁡(T′(h),T′′(h))=W(h)2M(h)3.
det(T′(h),T′′(h))=M(h)3W(h)2​.

So each MM-sign component of the dual curve is locally convex, and W=0W=0 does not create dual inflections; it only changes the speed along the same tangent direction. At a generic turning boundary, the dual arcs approach a common asymptote
m=−μb b+λb
m=−μb​b+λb​

from opposite sides. This gives a very clean picture of what the local turning-boundary theorem is really saying.
15. The natural global envelope functions are mj(b)mj​(b)

On each graph piece λj(μ)λj​(μ), for each tangent slope bb, the tangent intercept is
mj(b)=λj(μj(b))−bμj(b),λj′(μj(b))=b.
mj​(b)=λj​(μj​(b))−bμj​(b),λj′​(μj​(b))=b.

These satisfy the standard Legendre identities
mj′(b)=−μj(b),mj′′(b)=−1λj′′(μj(b)).
mj′​(b)=−μj​(b),mj′′​(b)=−λj′′​(μj​(b))1​.

So convex primal branches give concave dual envelopes and vice versa. Adjacent turning-boundary exclusion becomes a strict adjacent separation theorem for these envelope functions. But that strict adjacent separation is not enough to prevent nonadjacent re-entry. So the global obstruction is now very sharply reduced to recurrence of the envelope family, or equivalently recurrence of the slope function ββ.
16. Several tempting propagation theorems were tested and failed

We tried a number of “globalization by soft geometry” ideas and learned exactly where they break:

    “adjacent persistence of 22-secancy into the next branch” is too strong and essentially false in the abstract interval model;

    “first entry into support at a turning boundary forces tangency/kernel in a way that globalizes” is too strong in the naive form;

    “local convex dual arcs plus common asymptotes forbid same-parity nonadjacent intersections” is false in generic toy models;

    “positive Peano kernel implies enough variation-diminishing to globalize” is false in the strong form we wanted.

These failures are useful: they tell us the remaining gap is a genuinely missing global special-structure theorem, not just a proof we forgot to write down.
17. The forcing term for the slope equation is explicit, but not sign-definite

If
G:=W′+3(v5′v5−M′M)W,
G:=W′+3(v5​v5′​​−MM′​)W,

then
λμμμ=−v55M4G.
λμμμ​=−M4v55​​G.

Substituting the exact W′W′-identity shows that GG is still a linear combination of Δ7′′′,Δ7′,Δ7,Δ7′′′​,Δ7′​,Δ7​, and WW. So the forcing term is explicit, but there is no visible sign-definite structure or factorization miracle. This means the easy route “prove λμμμλμμμ​ has one sign and finish” also did not materialize.
18. On the highest-new slice, everything collapses to one scalar ϕϕ

This is the cleanest reduction of all. Let
ϕ:=λ[1].
ϕ:=λ[1].

Then on the highest-new slice,
Δ7[1]=v5 ϕ,
Δ7[1]​=v5​ϕ,

β[1]=ϕμ​,m[1]=ϕ−μϕμ​.

So the remaining highest-new geometry is exactly the affine geometry of one scalar function ϕ(μ)ϕ(μ). That is the most compressed form of the obstruction we found.
19. But even here, the easy sign route failed

In the minimal graded model,
ϕ∼κ eu (a2+ab−b2)a2b4(a+b)2,
ϕ∼κa2b4(a+b)2eu(a2+ab−b2)​,

so the direct highest-new scalar is explicit enough to prove survival, but not to prove one sign, because a2+ab−b2a2+ab−b2 changes sign with b/ab/a. This tells us the remaining obstruction is not going to die from a trivial sign argument on the highest-new coefficient alone.
20. So the real current goal line is no longer “prove zero-capture”

The live goal line of the brainstorm is now:

    locally, both generic boundary types are under control;

    the determinant kernel has genuine discrete sign structure on fixed-sign WW-intervals;

    the whole global problem has been reduced to a global propagation / non-recurrence theorem for either

        the slope function
        β(h)=−L(h)M(h),
        β(h)=−M(h)L(h)​,

        the dual tangent-line curve
        T(h)=(−LM,NM),
        T(h)=(−ML​,MN​),

That is the actual “goal line” now. The old blanket zero-capture framing is too coarse. What remains is a genuinely global special-structure theorem — probably RH-specific — ruling out slope / tangent-line re-entry on nonadjacent branches.
21. What this means for the paper update

If you are going to update the paper fully to match what we now know, the paper should say, in substance:

    the local W=0, M≠0W=0, M=0 problem is no longer “tangent separation”; it is affine-inflection geometry, and finite-order boundaries are locally pair-pair sterile;

    the local turning-boundary adjacent 2+22+2 problem is unconditionally closed;

    the determinant route is real, but only intervalwise unless a stronger propagation theorem is proved;

    the remaining global obstruction is recurrence of tangent-slope / tangent-line data across multiple branches, equivalently a global line-incidence problem for the (μ,λ)(μ,λ)-graph or the dual curve;

    the highest-new obstruction has collapsed to one explicit scalar ϕϕ, but the easy sign miracle failed.

That is, I think, the full math-form summary of what we have learned since the older “zero-capture” state.

\begin{definition}[Projective graph and dual tangent-line variables]
\label{def:mu-lambda-beta-m}
On the region where \(v_5\neq 0\), define
\[
\mu:=\frac{c}{v_5},
\qquad
\lambda:=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5}.
\]
On the subregion where \(M\neq 0\), define
\[
L:=v_5\Delta_7'-v_5'\Delta_7,
\qquad
\beta:=\frac{d\lambda}{d\mu},
\qquad
m:=\lambda-\mu\beta.
\]
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Closed minor system and dual tangent-line curve]
\label{prop:closed-minor-system-dual-curve}
Let
\[
F:=(c,v_5,\Delta_7),
\qquad
U:=(L,-N,M).
\]
Then
\[
F\times F'=U,
\qquad
U\times U'=W\,F.
\]
Equivalently,
\[
MN'-NM'=cW,
\qquad
ML'-LM'=v_5W,
\qquad
NL'-LN'=\Delta_7W.
\]

On the region where \(v_5M\neq 0\),
\[
\mu'=-\frac{M}{v_5^2},
\qquad
\beta=-\frac{L}{M},
\qquad
m=\frac{N}{M},
\]
and
\[
\beta'=-\frac{v_5W}{M^2},
\qquad
m'=\frac{cW}{M^2}.
\]
Hence the dual tangent-line curve
\[
T(h):=(\beta(h),m(h))
\]
satisfies
\[
T'(h)=\frac{W(h)}{M(h)^2}\,(-v_5(h),c(h)).
\]
Moreover,
\[
\det(T'(h),T''(h))=\frac{W(h)^2}{M(h)^3}.
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The identity
\[
F\times F'=(L,-N,M)
\]
is the direct expansion of the cross product. Differentiating gives
\[
U'=F\times F''.
\]
Applying the vector identity
\[
(A\times B)\times(A\times C)=\det(A,B,C)\,A
\]
with \(A=F\), \(B=F'\), \(C=F''\) yields
\[
U\times U'=(F\times F')\times(F\times F'')=\det(F,F',F'')\,F=W\,F,
\]
which is exactly the three displayed scalar identities.

Next,
\[
\mu'=\left(\frac{c}{v_5}\right)'
=\frac{c'v_5-cv_5'}{v_5^2}
=-\frac{M}{v_5^2},
\]
and
\[
\lambda'=\left(\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5}\right)'
=\frac{v_5\Delta_7'-v_5'\Delta_7}{v_5^2}
=\frac{L}{v_5^2},
\]
so
\[
\beta=\frac{\lambda'}{\mu'}=-\frac{L}{M}.
\]
Also
\[
\mu L+M\lambda
=
\frac{c}{v_5}(v_5\Delta_7'-v_5'\Delta_7)
+
(cv_5'-c'v_5)\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5}
=
c\Delta_7'-c'\Delta_7
=
N,
\]
hence
\[
m=\lambda-\mu\beta=\lambda+\mu\frac{L}{M}=\frac{N}{M}.
\]
The formulas for \(\beta'\) and \(m'\) follow immediately from
\[
ML'-LM'=v_5W,
\qquad
MN'-NM'=cW.
\]

Finally, write
\[
T'=\alpha V,
\qquad
\alpha:=\frac{W}{M^2},
\qquad
V:=(-v_5,c).
\]
Then
\[
\det(T',T'')=\alpha^2\det(V,V')
=\frac{W^2}{M^4}\det\!\begin{pmatrix}
-v_5 & -v_5'\\
c & c'
\end{pmatrix}
=
\frac{W^2}{M^3},
\]
because
\[
\det(V,V')=cv_5'-c'v_5=M.
\]
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Graph curvature identities in \((\mu,\lambda)\)-coordinates]
\label{cor:mu-lambda-curvature-identities}
On the region where \(v_5M\neq 0\),
\[
\lambda_{\mu\mu}=\frac{v_5^3}{M^3}W,
\]
and
\[
\lambda_{\mu\mu\mu}
=
-\frac{v_5^5}{M^4}
\left(
W'+3\left(\frac{v_5'}{v_5}-\frac{M'}{M}\right)W
\right).
\]
In particular, at a point where \(W=0\), \(M\neq 0\), and \(v_5\neq 0\),
\[
\lambda_{\mu\mu\mu}
=
-\frac{v_5^5}{M^4}W'.
\]
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Since
\[
\frac{d}{d\mu}=\frac{1}{\mu'}\frac{d}{dh}
=
-\frac{v_5^2}{M}\frac{d}{dh},
\]
the identity
\[
\lambda_{\mu\mu}=\frac{v_5^3}{M^3}W
\]
follows from
\[
\lambda_\mu=\beta,
\qquad
\beta'=-\frac{v_5W}{M^2}.
\]
Differentiating once more gives
\[
\lambda_{\mu\mu\mu}
=
-\frac{v_5^2}{M}\frac{d}{dh}\!\left(\frac{v_5^3}{M^3}W\right),
\]
which expands to the displayed formula. The last statement is the specialisation
\(W=0\).
\end{proof}

This is exact mathematics, not just roadmap language. It gives the paper the (μ,λ)(μ,λ), ββ, dual-curve, and order-77-still-not-99 structure in one clean place.

\begin{lemma}[Strip exclusion for \(K_{21}\) against a compact opposite branch]
\label{lem:strip-exclusion-k21}
Let \(I_1<I_2\) be adjacent ECT intervals meeting at a generic turning boundary
\[
M(h_b)=0,\qquad M'(h_b)\neq 0,\qquad N(h_b)\neq 0.
\]
Let \(J_1\Subset I_1\) be a compact subinterval. Then there exists a one-sided
neighborhood \(U_2\subset I_2\) of the shared boundary point \(h_b\) such that
\[
K_{21}(s,t):=\det(F(s),F'(s),F(t))\neq 0
\qquad
(s\in U_2,\ t\in J_1),
\]
where \(F(h)=(c(h),v_5(h),\Delta_7(h))\).
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Work in the affine chart
\[
x(h):=\frac{v_5(h)}{c(h)},
\qquad
y(h):=\frac{\Delta_7(h)}{c(h)}.
\]
At a generic turning boundary one has
\[
x'(h_b)=0,\qquad x''(h_b)\neq 0,\qquad y'(h_b)\neq 0.
\]
Hence \(y\) is a valid local coordinate and the normalized curve may be written
near \(h_b\) as a graph
\[
x=\chi(y)
\]
with
\[
\chi'(y_b)=0,\qquad \chi''(y_b)\neq 0.
\]
Thus \(x\) has a strict local extremum at the boundary, while the tangent slope
\[
m(h)=\frac{dy/dh}{dx/dh}=\frac{N(h)}{M(h)}
\]
blows up one-sidedly as \(h\to h_b\) from either adjacent interval.

Because \(J_1\Subset I_1\) is compact away from \(h_b\), there exists
\(\delta>0\) such that
\[
|x(t)-x(h_b)|\ge 2\delta
\qquad
(t\in J_1).
\]
After shrinking to a small one-sided neighborhood \(U_2\subset I_2\) of \(h_b\),
we may also assume
\[
|x(s)-x(h_b)|\le \delta
\qquad
(s\in U_2).
\]
Hence
\[
|x(t)-x(s)|\ge \delta
\qquad
(s\in U_2,\ t\in J_1).
\]

Fix a preliminary compact neighborhood \(U_2^0\Subset I_2\) of \(h_b\) and set
\[
B:=\sup\{|y(t)-y(s)|:\ t\in J_1,\ s\in U_2^0\}<\infty.
\]
Since \(m(s)\to \pm\infty\) as \(s\to h_b\) in \(I_2\), we may shrink further to
\(U_2\subset U_2^0\) so that
\[
|m(s)|>\frac{2B}{\delta}
\qquad
(s\in U_2).
\]

If \(K_{21}(s,t)=0\), then the tangent line at \(\Gamma(s)\) passes through
\(\Gamma(t)\), equivalently
\[
y(t)-y(s)=m(s)\bigl(x(t)-x(s)\bigr).
\]
Taking absolute values gives
\[
B\ge |y(t)-y(s)|=|m(s)|\,|x(t)-x(s)|>\frac{2B}{\delta}\cdot \delta=2B,
\]
a contradiction. Therefore \(K_{21}(s,t)\neq 0\) on \(U_2\times J_1\).
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Strip exclusion for \(K_{12}\) against a compact opposite branch]
\label{lem:strip-exclusion-k12}
Let \(I_1<I_2\) be adjacent ECT intervals meeting at a generic turning boundary
\[
M(h_b)=0,\qquad M'(h_b)\neq 0,\qquad N(h_b)\neq 0.
\]
Let \(J_2\Subset I_2\) be a compact subinterval. Then there exists a one-sided
neighborhood \(U_1\subset I_1\) of the shared boundary point \(h_b\) such that
\[
K_{12}(t,s):=\det(F(t),F'(t),F(s))\neq 0
\qquad
(t\in U_1,\ s\in J_2),
\]
where \(F(h)=(c(h),v_5(h),\Delta_7(h))\).
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
This is the left-right mirror of Lemma~\ref{lem:strip-exclusion-k21}.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Compact first-contact for \(K_{21}\)]
\label{lem:compact-first-contact-k21}
Let \(J_1\Subset I_1\), \(J_2\Subset I_2\) be compact subintervals across a
generic turning boundary. Assume there is a relatively open collar
\(V_2\subset J_2\) at the boundary-facing end of \(J_2\) such that
\[
K_{21}(s,t)\neq 0
\qquad
(s\in V_2,\ t\in J_1).
\]
Assume also that the zero set of \(K_{21}\) in \(J_2\times J_1\) is nonempty.
Then there exists a zero \((s_*,t_*)\in J_2\times J_1\) such that:
\begin{enumerate}
\item \(s_*\) is boundary-nearest in the \(x=v_5/c\) ordering among all
\(s\in J_2\) for which \(K_{21}(s,t)=0\) for some \(t\in J_1\);
\item
\[
\partial_t K_{21}(s_*,t_*)=0.
\]
\end{enumerate}
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Define
\[
A_{21}:=\{\,s\in J_2:\ \exists\, t\in J_1 \text{ with } K_{21}(s,t)=0\,\}.
\]
Since the zero set of \(K_{21}\) in \(J_2\times J_1\) is compact and nonempty,
the set \(A_{21}\) is compact and nonempty. By hypothesis,
\[
A_{21}\cap V_2=\varnothing.
\]
Hence \(A_{21}\) has a boundary-nearest element \(s_*\) in the \(x=v_5/c\)
ordering on \(J_2\). Choose \(t_*\in J_1\) with
\[
K_{21}(s_*,t_*)=0.
\]

Suppose
\[
\partial_t K_{21}(s_*,t_*)\neq 0.
\]
Then by the implicit function theorem there is a \(C^1\) local zero curve
\[
t=t(s)
\]
through \((s_*,t_*)\), defined for \(s\) near \(s_*\), such that
\[
K_{21}(s,t(s))=0.
\]
Because \(s_*\notin V_2\) and \(V_2\) is an open collar at the boundary-facing
end of \(J_2\), there exist nearby points \(s\in J_2\) that are boundary-nearer
than \(s_*\) in the \(x=v_5/c\) ordering. For such \(s\), the point
\((s,t(s))\) is also a zero of \(K_{21}\), contradicting the minimality of
\(s_*\). Therefore
\[
\partial_t K_{21}(s_*,t_*)=0.
\]
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Compact first-contact for \(K_{12}\)]
\label{lem:compact-first-contact-k12}
Let \(J_1\Subset I_1\), \(J_2\Subset I_2\) be compact subintervals across a
generic turning boundary. Assume there is a relatively open collar
\(V_1\subset J_1\) at the boundary-facing end of \(J_1\) such that
\[
K_{12}(t,s)\neq 0
\qquad
(t\in V_1,\ s\in J_2).
\]
Assume also that the zero set of \(K_{12}\) in \(J_1\times J_2\) is nonempty.
Then there exists a zero \((t_*,s_*)\in J_1\times J_2\) such that:
\begin{enumerate}
\item \(t_*\) is boundary-nearest in the \(x=v_5/c\) ordering among all
\(t\in J_1\) for which \(K_{12}(t,s)=0\) for some \(s\in J_2\);
\item
\[
\partial_s K_{12}(t_*,s_*)=0.
\]
\end{enumerate}
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Define
\[
A_{12}:=\{\,t\in J_1:\ \exists\, s\in J_2 \text{ with } K_{12}(t,s)=0\,\}.
\]
Since the zero set of \(K_{12}\) in \(J_1\times J_2\) is compact and nonempty,
the set \(A_{12}\) is compact and nonempty. By hypothesis,
\[
A_{12}\cap V_1=\varnothing.
\]
Hence \(A_{12}\) has a boundary-nearest element \(t_*\) in the \(x=v_5/c\)
ordering on \(J_1\). Choose \(s_*\in J_2\) with
\[
K_{12}(t_*,s_*)=0.
\]

Suppose
\[
\partial_s K_{12}(t_*,s_*)\neq 0.
\]
Then by the implicit function theorem there is a \(C^1\) local zero curve
\[
s=s(t)
\]
through \((t_*,s_*)\), defined for \(t\) near \(t_*\), such that
\[
K_{12}(t,s(t))=0.
\]
Because \(t_*\notin V_1\) and \(V_1\) is an open collar at the boundary-facing
end of \(J_1\), there exist nearby points \(t\in J_1\) that are boundary-nearer
than \(t_*\) in the \(x=v_5/c\) ordering. For such \(t\), the point
\((t,s(t))\) is also a zero of \(K_{12}\), contradicting the minimality of
\(t_*\). Therefore
\[
\partial_s K_{12}(t_*,s_*)=0.
\]
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[Adjacent pair-pair exclusion across a generic turning boundary]
\label{thm:adjacent-pair-pair-exclusion-turning}
Let \(I_1<I_2\) be adjacent ECT intervals meeting at a generic turning boundary
\[
M(h_b)=0,\qquad M'(h_b)\neq 0,\qquad N(h_b)\neq 0.
\]
Then no finite-slope affine line in the chart
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c},
\qquad
y=\frac{\Delta_7}{c}
\]
is \(2\)-secant to both \(\Gamma(I_1)\) and \(\Gamma(I_2)\).
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Assume for contradiction that a finite-slope line
\[
L:\ y=mx+b
\]
is \(2\)-secant to both adjacent branches. By
Lemma~\ref{lem:pair-pair-gives-directional-kernel-zero}, after removing a
small boundary neighborhood there exist compact subintervals
\[
J_1\Subset I_1,\qquad J_2\Subset I_2
\]
and a zero of one of the two directional kernels.

First suppose there exist \(s_0\in J_2\), \(t_0\in J_1\) such that
\[
K_{21}(s_0,t_0)=0.
\]
By Lemma~\ref{lem:strip-exclusion-k21}, there exists a one-sided neighborhood
\(U_2\subset I_2\) of \(h_b\) such that
\[
K_{21}(s,t)\neq 0
\qquad
(s\in U_2,\ t\in J_1).
\]
Choose a compact interval \(\widetilde J_2\Subset I_2\) containing \(s_0\) and
whose boundary-facing collar \(V_2\) lies in \(U_2\). Then the zero set of
\(K_{21}\) in \(\widetilde J_2\times J_1\) is nonempty, and
Lemma~\ref{lem:compact-first-contact-k21} yields a zero
\[
(s_*,t_*)\in \widetilde J_2\times J_1
\]
such that
\[
\partial_t K_{21}(s_*,t_*)=0.
\]
Together with \(K_{21}(s_*,t_*)=0\), this means that the tangent line at
\(\Gamma(s_*)\) is also tangent at \(\Gamma(t_*)\). Since
\(s_*\in I_2\) and \(t_*\in I_1\) are interior points, this gives a common
interior tangent slope across the adjacent branches, contradicting
Proposition~\ref{prop:adjacent-slope-range-separation}.

Now suppose instead there exist \(t_0\in J_1\), \(s_0\in J_2\) such that
\[
K_{12}(t_0,s_0)=0.
\]
By Lemma~\ref{lem:strip-exclusion-k12}, there exists a one-sided neighborhood
\(U_1\subset I_1\) of \(h_b\) such that
\[
K_{12}(t,s)\neq 0
\qquad
(t\in U_1,\ s\in J_2).
\]
Choose a compact interval \(\widetilde J_1\Subset I_1\) containing \(t_0\) and
whose boundary-facing collar \(V_1\) lies in \(U_1\). Then the zero set of
\(K_{12}\) in \(\widetilde J_1\times J_2\) is nonempty, and
Lemma~\ref{lem:compact-first-contact-k12} yields a zero
\[
(t_*,s_*)\in \widetilde J_1\times J_2
\]
such that
\[
\partial_s K_{12}(t_*,s_*)=0.
\]
Together with \(K_{12}(t_*,s_*)=0\), this means that the tangent line at
\(\Gamma(t_*)\) is also tangent at \(\Gamma(s_*)\). Again this gives a common
interior tangent slope across the adjacent branches, contradicting
Proposition~\ref{prop:adjacent-slope-range-separation}.

Both cases are impossible. Therefore no finite-slope line is \(2\)-secant to
both adjacent branches across a generic turning boundary.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[What the unconditional adjacent turning theorem does and does not yet replace]
\label{rem:status-adjacent-pair-pair-turning}
Theorem~\ref{thm:adjacent-pair-pair-exclusion-turning} gives an unconditional
exclusion of finite-slope pair-pair lines across a single generic turning
boundary. It is stronger than the older local directional-kernel reduction in
that it bypasses full symmetric zero-capture.

However, it does not by itself replace
Theorem~\ref{thm:partial-global-no-secant}. To obtain a full global no-four-secant
theorem from it, one would still need a separate propagation statement reducing
nonadjacent pair-pair lines to the adjacent turning-boundary case.
\end{remark}

This is the main missing theorem-level local update.

\begin{remark}[Current geometric bottleneck]

\begin{remark}[Current state of the argument]
\label{rem:current-state-of-argument}
The local one-pair analysis now consists of the canonical triple
\[
(c(h),\,v_5(h),\,\Delta_7(h)),
\]
together with the derived quantities
\[
M(h)=c(h)v_5'(h)-c'(h)v_5(h),
\qquad
N(h)=c(h)\Delta_7'(h)-c'(h)\Delta_7(h),
\]
\[
L(h)=v_5(h)\Delta_7'(h)-v_5'(h)\Delta_7(h),
\qquad
W(h)=\det(F(h),F'(h),F''(h)).
\]

On the region where \(v_5M\neq 0\), the projective graph variables
\[
\mu=\frac{c}{v_5},
\qquad
\lambda=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5}
\]
identify the normalized curve with a graph \(\lambda=\lambda(\mu)\), and
\[
\lambda_{\mu\mu}=\frac{v_5^3}{M^3}W,
\qquad
\beta:=\lambda_\mu=-\frac{L}{M},
\qquad
T(h)=\left(-\frac{L(h)}{M(h)},\frac{N(h)}{M(h)}\right).
\]
Thus the global line-incidence problem is equivalently a problem about the
recurrence of tangent slopes \(\beta\), or about vertical-line re-entry on the
dual tangent-line curve \(T\).

Locally, both generic boundary types are now under control. At finite-order
\(W=0,\ M\neq 0\) boundaries there is no local pair-pair birth, while at
generic turning boundaries actual adjacent pair-pair lines are excluded
unconditionally. The stronger symmetric directional-kernel theorem remains
available only conditionally on zero-capture and now serves as a sharper but
nonessential alternative route.

Accordingly, the remaining gap is no longer local boundary geometry. It is the
global propagation theorem linking these local facts: no fixed finite-slope line
should be able to leave and later re-enter the tangent-slope / tangent-line
data on nonadjacent branches. On the highest-new slice, this is the same as a
no-reentry theorem for the scalar graph
\[
\phi=\lambda^{[1]},
\qquad
\beta^{[1]}=\phi_\mu,
\qquad
m^{[1]}=\phi-\mu\phi_\mu.
\]
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Equivalent formulations of the remaining global problem]
\label{rem:equivalent-global-propagation-problem}
On a generic component, the remaining missing theorem may be formulated in any
of the following equivalent ways:
\begin{enumerate}
\item no finite-slope affine line in the chart
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c},
\qquad
y=\frac{\Delta_7}{c}
\]
is \(2\)-secant to two nonadjacent ECT intervals;

\item the slope function
\[
\beta(h):=-\frac{L(h)}{M(h)},
\qquad
L=v_5\Delta_7'-v_5'\Delta_7,
\]
does not revisit a level on nonadjacent branches;

\item the dual tangent-line curve
\[
T(h)=\left(-\frac{L(h)}{M(h)},\frac{N(h)}{M(h)}\right)
\]
has no nonadjacent same-parity re-entry against a vertical line in the
\((b,m)\)-plane;

\item on the highest-new slice, the scalar graph
\[
\phi=\lambda^{[1]}
\]
has no nonadjacent re-entry of its slope \(\phi_\mu\).
\end{enumerate}
The results proved above resolve the local behavior at finite-order
\(W=0,\ M\neq 0\) boundaries and at generic turning boundaries; what remains is
the global propagation theorem linking these local facts.
\end{remark}

G. One last optional insertion if you want the determinant “goodie” visible

This is not necessary, but if you want to capture the “intervalwise determinant sign law” insight without overcommitting to a full theorem about propagation, insert this as a remark immediately after cor:mu-lambda-curvature-identities:

\begin{remark}[Determinant interpretation on a fixed-sign \(W\)-interval]
\label{rem:determinant-interpretation-fixed-sign-W}
On any connected interval where \(c\), \(M\), and \(W\) are nonzero and \(W\)
keeps one sign, the graph \(\lambda=\lambda(\mu)\) is strictly convex or
strictly concave. Consequently, for any ordered triple of distinct points on
that interval, the determinant
\[
D(s,t,u)=\det(F(s),F(t),F(u))
\]
has the corresponding fixed Vandermonde sign. Thus the unresolved global issue
is not intervalwise sign regularity, but propagation across turning seams and
possible nonadjacent recurrence of tangent-slope / tangent-line data.
\end{remark}

Insert this LaTeX

\begin{proposition}[Local determinant sign transport across a generic turning boundary]
\label{prop:local-determinant-sign-transport-turning}
Let \(h_b\) be a generic turning boundary:
\[
M(h_b)=0,\qquad M'(h_b)\neq 0,\qquad N(h_b)\neq 0.
\]
Then there exists a neighborhood \(U\) of \(h_b\) and a sign
\(\sigma_{\mathrm{turn}}\in\{\pm 1\}\) such that for any three distinct points
\(h_1,h_2,h_3\in U\),
\[
\operatorname{sgn} D(h_1,h_2,h_3)
=
\sigma_{\mathrm{turn}}\,
\operatorname{sgn}\bigl((h_2-h_1)(h_3-h_1)(h_3-h_2)\bigr),
\]
where
\[
D(h_1,h_2,h_3):=\det(F(h_1),F(h_2),F(h_3)),
\qquad
F=(c,v_5,\Delta_7).
\]
Equivalently, the triple \((c,v_5,\Delta_7)\) is locally discretely sign-regular
of order \(3\) across a generic turning boundary.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Work in the normalized affine chart
\[
x(h):=\frac{v_5(h)}{c(h)},
\qquad
y(h):=\frac{\Delta_7(h)}{c(h)}.
\]
At a generic turning boundary one has
\[
x'(h_b)=0,\qquad x''(h_b)\neq 0,\qquad y'(h_b)\neq 0.
\]
Hence \(y\) is a valid local coordinate near \(h_b\), and the normalized curve
may be written as
\[
x=\chi(y)
\]
with
\[
\chi'(y_b)=0,\qquad \chi''(y_b)\neq 0.
\]
After shrinking \(U\), the sign of \(\chi''\) is constant on \(U\).

Now for \(h_i\in U\), write
\[
x_i:=x(h_i),\qquad y_i:=y(h_i).
\]
Since
\[
F(h_i)=c(h_i)\,(1,x_i,y_i),
\]
we have
\[
D(h_1,h_2,h_3)
=
c(h_1)c(h_2)c(h_3)\,
\det\!\begin{pmatrix}
1&x_1&y_1\\
1&x_2&y_2\\
1&x_3&y_3
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
Using \(x_i=\chi(y_i)\), the \(3\times 3\) determinant factors as
\[
\det\!\begin{pmatrix}
1&x_1&y_1\\
1&x_2&y_2\\
1&x_3&y_3
\end{pmatrix}
=
(y_2-y_1)(y_3-y_1)(y_3-y_2)\,\chi[y_1,y_2,y_3],
\]
where \(\chi[y_1,y_2,y_3]\) is the second divided difference of \(\chi\).
By the scalar divided-difference mean-value theorem,
\[
\chi[y_1,y_2,y_3]=\frac12\,\chi''(\eta)
\]
for some \(\eta\) between the \(y_i\). Thus \(\chi[y_1,y_2,y_3]\) has fixed sign
on \(U\).

Also \(c\) has fixed sign on a sufficiently small neighborhood of \(h_b\), and
since \(y'(h_b)\neq 0\), the map \(h\mapsto y(h)\) is monotone on \(U\). Hence
\[
\operatorname{sgn}\bigl((y_2-y_1)(y_3-y_1)(y_3-y_2)\bigr)
=
\operatorname{sgn}(y')^3\,
\operatorname{sgn}\bigl((h_2-h_1)(h_3-h_1)(h_3-h_2)\bigr),
\]
with \(\operatorname{sgn}(y')\) constant on \(U\).

Collecting the fixed signs of \(c\), \(y'\), and \(\chi''\) gives the desired
constant \(\sigma_{\mathrm{turn}}\).
\end{proof}

This theorem is exactly the theorem-level version of the later local turning-boundary determinant-sign transport result.

Insert this LaTeX

\begin{proposition}[Dual asymptote at a generic turning boundary]
\label{prop:dual-asymptote-turning-boundary}
Let \(h_b\) be a generic turning boundary:
\[
M(h_b)=0,\qquad M'(h_b)\neq 0,\qquad N(h_b)\neq 0.
\]
Assume \(v_5(h_b)\neq 0\), and write
\[
\mu_b:=\frac{c(h_b)}{v_5(h_b)},
\qquad
\lambda_b:=\frac{\Delta_7(h_b)}{v_5(h_b)}.
\]
Let
\[
T(h)=\bigl(\beta(h),m(h)\bigr)
=
\left(-\frac{L(h)}{M(h)},\frac{N(h)}{M(h)}\right)
\]
be the dual tangent-line curve on the neighboring \(M\neq 0\) branches.
Then both one-sided dual arcs have the common asymptote
\[
m=-\mu_b\,\beta+\lambda_b,
\]
and, more precisely,
\[
m+\mu_b\beta-\lambda_b
=
\frac{1}{4a\,\beta}+o\!\left(\frac1\beta\right)
\qquad\text{as } |\beta|\to\infty,
\]
where \(a\neq 0\) is the quadratic coefficient in the local turning-point normal
form
\[
\mu-\mu_b=a(\lambda-\lambda_b)^2+O((\lambda-\lambda_b)^3).
\]
In particular, the two adjacent dual arcs approach the same asymptote from
opposite sides.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
At a generic turning boundary one has \(\mu'(h_b)=0\) and \(\lambda'(h_b)\neq 0\),
so \(\lambda\) is a valid local coordinate and
\[
\mu-\mu_b=a(\lambda-\lambda_b)^2+O((\lambda-\lambda_b)^3),
\qquad a\neq 0.
\]
Differentiating gives
\[
\frac{d\mu}{d\lambda}=2a(\lambda-\lambda_b)+O((\lambda-\lambda_b)^2),
\]
hence
\[
\beta=\frac{d\lambda}{d\mu}
=
\frac{1}{2a(\lambda-\lambda_b)}+O(1).
\]
Thus \(|\beta|\to\infty\) as \(h\to h_b\) from either side.

Now
\[
m=\lambda-\mu\beta,
\]
so
\[
m+\mu_b\beta-\lambda_b
=
(\lambda-\lambda_b)-(\mu-\mu_b)\beta.
\]
Using
\[
\mu-\mu_b=a(\lambda-\lambda_b)^2+O((\lambda-\lambda_b)^3)
\]
and
\[
\beta=\frac{1}{2a(\lambda-\lambda_b)}+O(1),
\]
we obtain
\[
(\mu-\mu_b)\beta
=
\frac12(\lambda-\lambda_b)+O((\lambda-\lambda_b)^2).
\]
Therefore
\[
m+\mu_b\beta-\lambda_b
=
\frac12(\lambda-\lambda_b)+O((\lambda-\lambda_b)^2).
\]
Substituting
\[
\lambda-\lambda_b=\frac{1}{2a\beta}+o\!\left(\frac1\beta\right)
\]
gives
\[
m+\mu_b\beta-\lambda_b
=
\frac{1}{4a\,\beta}+o\!\left(\frac1\beta\right).
\]
Since \(\beta\to+\infty\) on one side and \(\beta\to-\infty\) on the other, the
correction term changes sign, so the two one-sided dual arcs approach the same
asymptote from opposite sides.
\end{proof}

This is exactly the “dual asymptote theorem” from the later attack.

\begin{remark}[Audit: what the current local theory does \emph{not} imply]
\label{rem:audit-no-easy-globalization}
Several tempting globalization statements suggested by the local theory are too
strong in generic models and should not be assumed without further RH-specific
input.

\begin{enumerate}
\item Naive support propagation is not enough: exclusion of adjacent pair-pair
lines does not by itself force exclusion for nonadjacent pairs.

\item Local convexity of the dual tangent-line curve, even together with the
shared asymptote structure of
Proposition~\ref{prop:dual-asymptote-turning-boundary}, is not by itself enough
to forbid nonadjacent same-parity re-entry in the dual \((\beta,m)\)-plane.

\item The direct highest-new septic coefficient is explicit enough to prove
noncancellation, but not generically one-signed. Thus no trivial sign theorem
for the scalar graph \(\phi=\lambda^{[1]}\) should be expected without further
RH-specific structure.
\end{enumerate}

Accordingly, the remaining gap is now a genuinely global special-structure
theorem, not a missing local lemma.
\end{remark}

This captures the strongest negative conclusion from the later exploration. It is important because otherwise the draft still invites readers to think “there must just be one more local propagation lemma.”

Yes. Matching our running brainstorm, not the older zero-capture framing, here is the cleanest summary of what we now know since the last paper draft.

The biggest change is architectural. The problem is no longer “prove zero-capture and the rest follows.” The work has split into three layers: the direct order-77 / septic algebra for the canonical second residual Δ7Δ7​; the local geometry at W=0, M≠0W=0, M=0 and at generic turning boundaries; and the genuinely global line-incidence / propagation problem for the normalized one-pair curve and its derived slope/dual objects. In particular, the real global obstruction is now understood as a non-recurrence problem, not a missing local lemma.

On the algebraic side, the old “use septic trace” idea was abandoned. The correct order-77 object is the fixed-sector class
[A7f]∈f/CA5f,
[A7f​]∈f/CA5f​,

or equivalently the determinant
Δ7:=u7v5−u5v7.
Δ7​:=u7​v5​−u5​v7​.

The direct q(7)q(7)-driven K1K1​-transport slice is II-directional, the quintic fixed-sector vector has generically nonzero SS-component v5v5​, and therefore the direct q(7)q(7)-driven contribution to Δ7Δ7​ is generically nonzero. So the septic residual is real, canonical at the right level, and not a fake witness. That is a major step beyond the older draft.

More sharply, on the highest-new slice the surviving scalar has already been reduced to the direct q(7)q(7)-combination
ϕ=λ[1]=κ((x2−x1)ν6(q(7))+v(γ5−α5)(q(7))),
ϕ=λ[1]=κ((x2​−x1​)ν6(q(7))​+v(γ5​−α5​)(q(7))),

and in the minimal graded model its coefficient is explicit enough to prove noncancellation. But that same computation also killed the easiest remaining miracle: the coefficient is not generically one-signed, so the path “highest-new scalar has fixed sign, therefore the geometry globalizes” is no longer believable in naive form. The highest-new slice survives, but it does not immediately collapse the global problem.

On the W=0, M≠0W=0, M=0 side, the local geometry has been clarified completely. In the affine chart
x=v5c,y=Δ7c,
x=cv5​​,y=cΔ7​​,

so a generic W=0, M≠0W=0, M=0 boundary is an ordinary affine inflection unless extra structure forces W′(hb)=0W′(hb​)=0. That means the old tangent-separator route really does fail generically there. But the later determinant analysis showed something better: finite-order W=0, M≠0W=0, M=0 boundaries are locally sterile for pair-pair birth. So W=0W=0 is not a local multi-secant explosion zone; it is a place where the old proof mechanism fails but local 2+22+2 birth does not occur.

The turning-boundary side also improved a lot. We now have a genuine bypass of full symmetric zero-capture: strip exclusion against a compact opposite branch, compact first-contact, and first-contact-implies-tangency together give unconditional adjacent pair-pair exclusion across a generic turning boundary. In other words, the local turning-boundary geometry is no longer the main problem. The stronger symmetric directional-kernel theorem still exists conditionally on zero-capture, but actual adjacent 2+22+2 lines are already blocked without needing the old full zero-capture package.

The determinant route turned out to be real, but subtler than first hoped. There is an exact mean-value / Peano-kernel theorem for
D(s,t,u)=det⁡(F(s),F(t),F(u)),F=(c,v5,Δ7),
D(s,t,u)=det(F(s),F(t),F(u)),F=(c,v5​,Δ7​),

and on intervals where WW has fixed sign this gives local discrete order-33 sign regularity. So the determinant route is not heuristic. But the naive “positive kernel ⇒⇒ enough variation-diminishing to globalize” argument fails in the form we wanted. So it gave a real local theorem and a better conceptual framework, but not the missing global propagation theorem.

The best geometric reformulation we found is in the projective graph variables
μ=cv5,λ=Δ7v5.

So WW is exactly graph curvature up to a nowhere-zero factor. This turns the one-pair geometry into ordinary graph geometry: WW-sign pieces are convex/concave graph pieces, finite-order W=0W=0 are ordinary inflections, and the global obstruction becomes a line-incidence problem for a piecewise convex/concave graph.

The true scalar slope variable is

The dual tangent-line curve makes this even more geometric. Define

But it also clarified the remaining limitation: local convex dual arcs plus shared asymptotes are still not enough by themselves to rule out nonadjacent same-parity re-entry. So the gap is genuinely global, not a hidden local lemma.

A lot of the negative information is just as important. So the remaining theorem is not “one more local propagation lemma.” It is a genuinely global special-structure theorem — either non-recurrence of ββ, or no vertical-line re-entry for the dual curve TT, or a strongest-possible version on the highest-new scalar graph ϕϕ.

here's what the other chat, working on finite/bad core endgame did:

This is very good. It materially sharpens the finite/bad-core route, and I think it changes the roadmap in a useful way. The key gain is that it separates the lifted local problem into three regimes instead of treating all TvTv​-zeros the same:

    finite-order Kv=0Kv​=0: locally sterile for lifted 33-point birth;

    finite-order Tv=0Tv​=0 with Kv≠0Kv​=0: locally sterile for lifted 44-point birth;

    mixed Kv=Tv=0Kv​=Tv​=0: genuinely different, with a codimension-two monomial normal form whose leading 44-point determinant is a generalized Vandermonde and can admit opposite-side quadruples.

That is a real structural improvement. It means the lifted route is no longer “generic local birth everywhere until proven otherwise.” Generic finite-order local birth is now mostly under control, and the remaining lifted obstruction is sharply localized to:

    global recurrence / re-entry,

    possible infinite-order flatness,

    and the mixed normal-form case Kv=Tv=0Kv​=Tv​=0.

I think the most important new conclusion in that summary is exactly this:

    a blanket theorem “finite-order isolated Tv=0Tv​=0 boundaries are locally sterile” is false; the mixed case is a genuine codimension-two obstruction.

That is the kind of negative result that saves a lot of wasted time. It tells us not to keep pushing a false universal local sterility theorem on the lifted side.

So, strategically, I would now update the hierarchy of attacks like this.

First priority: formalize the two lifted sterility theorems that now look real.

Those are:

    finite-order isolated Kv=0Kv​=0 implies local sterility for lifted 33-point birth;

    finite-order isolated Tv=0Tv​=0 with Kv≠0Kv​=0 implies local sterility for lifted 44-point birth.

Those should become theorem-level statements in the paper, because they are exactly parallel to the new W=0W=0 story on the one-pair side and they cleanly remove generic local lifted birth as the main obstruction.

Second priority: make the mixed case explicit as the remaining local lifted obstruction.

I would not bury it in a remark. I would surface it as an audit/proposition-level statement:

    after affine normalization, the mixed boundary reduces to
    Qv(x)∼(xn,x,xm),
    Qv​(x)∼(xn,x,xm),

    the leading coplanarity determinant is the generalized Vandermonde for exponents
    0,1,m,n,
    0,1,m,n,

    and this model can genuinely admit opposite-side quadruples for some patterns, so the mixed case is not killed by the same first-contact argument.

That tells the reader exactly where the local lifted route stops.

Third priority: decide whether the actual zeta geometry can realize the dangerous mixed patterns (m,n)(m,n).

To me, this is now the cleanest next theorem target on the lifted side. The question is no longer generic local birth. It is:

    does the actual one-pair zeta geometry permit the mixed normal forms whose generalized Vandermonde admits opposite-side coplanar quadruples?

If the answer is no, the lifted route gets dramatically cleaner. If the answer is yes, then the mixed case becomes the one genuine local obstruction that the global endgame must carry.

Fourth priority: keep the quantitative defect-thickened strengthened coincidence route in parallel, but I would now treat it as the global bridge, not the immediate local attack.

That route is still valuable because it says bad two-pair cores force near-coincidence of the strengthened invariant Ψ^Ψ
. But the new lifted summary tells us the local geometric side is now more sharply stratified than we previously thought. So I would use the quantitative coincidence theorem to force bad cores into the close-point regime, and then use the lifted stratification:

    generic close-point bad cores are killed by the KvKv​- and TvTv​-sterility theorems,

    only mixed Kv=Tv=0Kv​=Tv​=0 close-point cores remain.

That is a much cleaner endgame split than before.

So my current ranking is:

    write/prove the KvKv​-sterility theorem;

    write/prove the TvTv​-sterility theorem under Kv≠0Kv​=0;

    isolate the mixed normal-form invariants (m,n)(m,n) and test whether the dangerous patterns are realizable in the actual geometry;

    in parallel, prove the quantitative defect-thickened strengthened coincidence theorem to force bad two-pair cores into this local lifted classification.

That is now cleaner than the old one-pair ββ-route, because it replaces a vague global recurrence problem by a much more structured dichotomy: generic local lifted birth is gone, and the remaining local obstruction is a specific codimension-two mixed model.

So my bottom line is:

Yes, this is a real advance, and it changes the route.

Then define the pure 44-body interaction remainder by inclusion–exclusion, subtracting all 11-, 22-, and 33-atom contributions. If that source-level object exists, then three kinds of conditions should become formal:

First, full label symmetry under permuting the four atoms.

Second, collapse on partial diagonals: whenever two atoms coincide, the 44-atom source reduces to a 33-atom source, so the pure 44-body remainder should vanish.

Third, vanishing when any amplitude is zero.

Those are the exact 44-point analogues of the 22-point structural conditions in the note. And if they hold, then the pure 44-body remainder should inherit very strong divisibility:

    by ∏jaj∏j​aj​ from amplitude collapse,

    and by every pair difference hi−hjhi​−hj​ from partial-diagonal collapse.

Because the object is symmetric, vanishing on each partial diagonal should force divisibility by the discriminant
∏i<j(hi−hj)2
i<j∏​(hi​−hj​)2

rather than just a single linear factor. That is the 44-point analogue of the midpoint/separation evenness argument in the 22-point note. I would not claim this as proved yet, but structurally it is exactly the kind of theorem to attack.

And this would be a big deal, because it would give the extra algebraic condition you asked for:

    a true bad 44-point core is not merely coplanar on QvQv​; it lies on a coplanarity branch along which a much more singular source-level 44-body remainder vanishes.

That is exactly the kind of restriction that a generic local branch sheet like the nonmixed odd-order model
Q(x)=(x4,x,x2)
Q(x)=(x4,x,x2)

will probably not satisfy automatically.

So my answer is:

    Yes, this helps the 44-point attack conceptually.

    It does not solve the 44-point branch directly.

    But it points to the right missing theorem: a source-level 44-body interaction remainder theorem.

That is now the cleanest way I see to derive an extra algebraic condition beyond coplanarity.

The exact next attack I would make is:

    define the raw pure 44-body interaction remainder by inclusion–exclusion from the source-level corrected map;

    prove it is symmetric, vanishes when any amplitude is zero, and vanishes on every partial diagonal hi=hjhi​=hj​;

    deduce discriminant-type divisibility;

    then test whether the unique nonmixed odd-order branch sheet and the mixed normal form can satisfy the resulting higher-order vanishing.

That is the strongest way this note helps the 44-pair side.

\begin{proposition}[Conditional source-level quadratic interaction factorization]
\label{prop:conditional-source-level-quadratic-two-pair}
Assume there exists a finite-dimensional complex vector space \(\mathcal G\) and
an analytic corrected quotient-germ map
\[
\mathfrak Q:\mu\longmapsto \mathfrak Q(\mu)\in \mathcal G
\]
defined on small finite atomic sources
\[
\mu=\sum_j a_j\delta_{h_j},
\]
such that
\[
\mathcal F_1(a,h):=\mathfrak Q(a\delta_h),
\qquad
\mathcal F_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2):=\mathfrak Q(a_1\delta_{h_1}+a_2\delta_{h_2}),
\]
and such that the cubic, quintic, and septic quotient defects are obtained by
fixed linear projections from the raw interaction remainder
\[
\mathcal I(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2):=
\mathcal F_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)-\mathcal F_1(a_1,h_1)-\mathcal F_1(a_2,h_2).
\]

Assume moreover that:
\begin{enumerate}
\item \(\mathcal F_2\) is symmetric under swapping the two labeled atoms;
\item \(\mathcal F_2(0,h_1;a_2,h_2)=\mathcal F_1(a_2,h_2)\) and
\(\mathcal F_2(a_1,h_1;0,h_2)=\mathcal F_1(a_1,h_1)\);
\item \(\mathcal F_2(a_1,h;a_2,h)=\mathcal F_1(a_1+a_2,h)\).
\end{enumerate}

Then there exists an analytic \(\mathcal G\)-valued germ
\[
\mathcal J(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
\]
such that
\[
\mathcal I(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
=
a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\,\mathcal J(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2).
\]
Consequently the raw cubic, quintic, and septic quotient defects satisfy
\[
\mathcal E^{(3)}=a_1a_2\,O(\delta^2),
\qquad
\mathcal E^{(5)}=a_1a_2\,O(\delta^2),
\qquad
\overline{\mathcal E}^{(7)}=a_1a_2\,O(\delta^2),
\qquad
\delta:=|h_1-h_2|,
\]
uniformly on compacta.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By the one-amplitude collapse assumption, \(\mathcal I\) vanishes when
\(a_1=0\) or \(a_2=0\). By analyticity, it is divisible by \(a_1a_2\):
\[
\mathcal I(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)=a_1a_2\,G(h_1,h_2)
\]
for some analytic \(\mathcal G\)-valued germ \(G\).

By symmetry of \(\mathcal F_2\), the function \(G\) is symmetric:
\[
G(h_1,h_2)=G(h_2,h_1).
\]
By the diagonal collapse assumption,
\[
G(h,h)=0.
\]

Now pass to midpoint/separation variables
\[
m:=\frac{h_1+h_2}{2},
\qquad
s:=h_2-h_1.
\]
Then
\[
\widetilde G(m,s):=G\!\left(m-\frac s2,m+\frac s2\right)
\]
is analytic, even in \(s\), and vanishes at \(s=0\). Hence
\[
\widetilde G(m,s)=s^2H(m,s)
\]
for some analytic \(\mathcal G\)-valued germ \(H\). Returning to
\((h_1,h_2)\) gives the claimed factorization
\[
\mathcal I(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)=a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\,\mathcal J(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2).
\]

Since the raw cubic, quintic, and septic quotient defects are obtained by fixed
linear projections from \(\mathcal I\), the same quadratic separation factor
passes to each raw defect.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Conditional closure of the two-point branch on good patches]
\label{cor:conditional-two-point-closure-good-patches}
Assume the hypotheses of
Proposition~\ref{prop:conditional-source-level-quadratic-two-pair}, and assume
also that the normalized amplitudes remain bounded on compact good patches.
Then the normalized defects satisfy
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}=O(\delta^2),
\qquad
E_{12}^{(5)}=O(\delta^2),
\qquad
\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}=O(\delta^2),
\qquad
\delta:=|h_1-h_2|.
\]
Consequently, on any compact interval
\[
J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\},
\]
there is no nontrivial normalized bad two-point core with sufficiently small
separation \(|h_1-h_2|\).
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
The quadratic estimates follow by dividing the raw defects by \(a_1\), using
bounded normalized amplitudes.

By Corollary~\ref{cor:bad-two-pair-cores-defect-scale-close},
\[
|h_1-h_2|
\le
C_J\Bigl(
|E_{12}^{(3)}|+\|E_{12}^{(5)}\|+\bigl|\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}\bigr|
\Bigr)
\]
on \(J\). The quadratic defect estimate therefore gives
\[
|h_1-h_2|\le C'_J\,|h_1-h_2|^2,
\]
which is impossible for sufficiently small nonzero \(|h_1-h_2|\).
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Shrinking exact lifted three-point circuits concentrate into \(K_v=0\)]
\label{prop:shrinking-exact-lifted-three-point-circuits}
Let \(P\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ v_5\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}\) be compact, and write
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c},
\qquad
S=\sigma_v=\frac{\Delta_7}{cv_5}.
\]
For distinct \(x_1,x_2,x_3\), define
\[
\Delta_3(x_1,x_2,x_3):=
\det\!\begin{pmatrix}
1&x_1&S(x_1)\\
1&x_2&S(x_2)\\
1&x_3&S(x_3)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
Then:
\begin{enumerate}
\item if \(\Delta_3(x_{1,n},x_{2,n},x_{3,n})=0\) for a sequence of distinct
triples with \(x_{j,n}\to x_*\), then \(K_v(x_*)=0\);
\item if \(P_0\Subset P\) is compact and disjoint from \(\{K_v=0\}\), then
there exists \(\rho_3>0\) such that no exact lifted three-point circuit in
\(P_0\) has \(x\)-diameter \(<\rho_3\).
\end{enumerate}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
One has the standard factorization
\[
\Delta_3(x_1,x_2,x_3)
=
V_3(x_1,x_2,x_3)\,S[x_1,x_2,x_3],
\]
where
\[
V_3(x_1,x_2,x_3)=(x_2-x_1)(x_3-x_1)(x_3-x_2)
\]
and \(S[x_1,x_2,x_3]\) is the second divided difference of \(S\). For distinct
nodes, \(V_3\neq 0\), so \(\Delta_3=0\) implies
\[
S[x_1,x_2,x_3]=0.
\]
As \(x_1,x_2,x_3\to x_*\),
\[
S[x_1,x_2,x_3]\to \frac12 S''(x_*).
\]
Since \(K_v\) is the lifted curvature numerator for \(\Lambda_v=(x,S)\), it is
\(S''\) up to a nowhere-zero factor in the \(x\)-coordinate. This proves (1).
Assertion (2) follows by compactness.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Repeated-node tangent-line bridge for the lifted three-point branch]
\label{lem:repeated-node-tangent-line-bridge}
With the notation above, define
\[
\Delta_3(a,b,u):=
\det\!\begin{pmatrix}
1&a&S(a)\\
1&b&S(b)\\
1&u&S(u)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
Then
\[
\frac{\Delta_3(a,b,u)}{b-a}
\longrightarrow
\det\!\begin{pmatrix}
1&a&S(a)\\
0&1&S'(a)\\
1&u&S(u)
\end{pmatrix}
\qquad (b\to a).
\]
Equivalently, if an exact lifted three-point circuit has one collapsing pair,
its limit is a tangent-line contact configuration for the planar lifted curve
\[
\Lambda_v=(x,S).
\]
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Differentiate the second row with respect to \(b\) and pass to the limit.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Local branch classification near a finite-order \(K_v\)-zero]
\label{prop:local-model-kv-branch-classification}
Let \(x=0\) be an isolated finite-order zero of \(K_v\) on a good \(v_5\)-patch.
After an affine normalization of the target preserving collinearity, write
\[
S(x)=x^m+O(x^{m+1}),
\qquad
m\ge 3.
\]
Then the repeated-node tangent-line contact equation
\[
S(u)-S(a)-S'(a)(u-a)=0
\]
has the following local opposite-side classification for \(a<0<u\):
\begin{enumerate}
\item if \(m\) is even, there is no opposite-side branch near \(0\);
\item if \(m\) is odd, there is exactly one smooth opposite-side branch
\[
u=u(a)
\]
for \(a<0\) sufficiently small, and
\[
\frac{u(a)}{-a}\longrightarrow \lambda_m,
\]
where \(\lambda_m>1\) is the unique positive root of
\[
\lambda^m-m\lambda-(m-1)=0.
\]
\end{enumerate}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Write \(a=-\alpha<0\), \(u=\lambda\alpha>0\). For the model \(S(x)=x^m\),
the equation becomes
\[
\lambda^m+m\lambda+(m-1)=0
\]
if \(m\) is even, and
\[
\lambda^m-m\lambda-(m-1)=0
\]
if \(m\) is odd. The even case has no positive root. In the odd case, the
polynomial
\[
P_m(\lambda):=\lambda^m-m\lambda-(m-1)
\]
satisfies \(P_m(1)=-2(m-1)<0\), \(P_m(\lambda)\to+\infty\), and
\[
P_m'(\lambda)=m(\lambda^{m-1}-1),
\]
so it has a unique positive root \(\lambda_m>1\). The general normalized germ
\(S(x)=x^m+O(x^{m+1})\) is then handled by the implicit function theorem.
\end{proof}

K_v=0.

\begin{proposition}[Shrinking exact lifted four-point circuits concentrate into \(T_v=0\)]
\label{prop:shrinking-exact-lifted-four-point-circuits}
Let \(P\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ v_5\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}\) be compact, and write
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c},
\qquad
Y=\frac{u_5}{c},
\qquad
S=\sigma_v=\frac{\Delta_7}{cv_5}.
\]
For distinct \(x_1,x_2,x_3,x_4\), define
\[
\Delta_4(x_1,x_2,x_3,x_4):=
\det\!\begin{pmatrix}
1&Y(x_1)&x_1&S(x_1)\\
1&Y(x_2)&x_2&S(x_2)\\
1&Y(x_3)&x_3&S(x_3)\\
1&Y(x_4)&x_4&S(x_4)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
Then:
\begin{enumerate}
\item if \(\Delta_4(x_{1,n},x_{2,n},x_{3,n},x_{4,n})=0\) for a sequence of
distinct quadruples with \(x_{j,n}\to x_*\), then \(T_v(x_*)=0\);
\item if \(P_0\Subset P\) is compact and disjoint from \(\{T_v=0\}\), then
there exists \(\rho_4>0\) such that no exact lifted four-point circuit in
\(P_0\) has \(x\)-diameter \(<\rho_4\).
\end{enumerate}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
There is a standard generalized divided-difference factorization
\[
\Delta_4(x_1,x_2,x_3,x_4)
=
V_4(x_1,x_2,x_3,x_4)\,\mathcal D_4(x_1,x_2,x_3,x_4),
\]
where \(V_4\) is the ordinary Vandermonde. As all four nodes coalesce,
\[
\mathcal D_4(x_1,x_2,x_3,x_4)\to \frac1{12}W_x(1,Y,x,S)(x_*)=\frac1{12}T_v(x_*).
\]
For distinct nodes \(V_4\neq 0\), so \(\Delta_4=0\) implies
\(\mathcal D_4=0\), hence \(T_v(x_*)=0\) in the limit. Assertion (2) follows by
compactness.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Repeated-node tangent-plane bridge for the lifted four-point branch]
\label{lem:repeated-node-tangent-plane-bridge}
With the notation above, define
\[
\Delta_4(a,b,u,v):=
\det\!\begin{pmatrix}
1&Y(a)&a&S(a)\\
1&Y(b)&b&S(b)\\
1&Y(u)&u&S(u)\\
1&Y(v)&v&S(v)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
Then
\[
\frac{\Delta_4(a,b,u,v)}{b-a}
\longrightarrow
\det\!\begin{pmatrix}
1&Y(a)&a&S(a)\\
0&Y'(a)&1&S'(a)\\
1&Y(u)&u&S(u)\\
1&Y(v)&v&S(v)
\end{pmatrix}
\qquad (b\to a).
\]
Equivalently, if an exact lifted four-point circuit has one collapsing pair, its
limit is a tangent-plane contact configuration for the lifted space curve
\[
Q_v=(Y,x,S).
\]
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Differentiate the second row with respect to \(b\) and pass to the limit.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Progress on the nonmixed lifted four-point branch]
\label{rem:progress-nonmixed-four-point-branch}
At a nonmixed lifted point
\[
T_v(0)=0,\qquad K_v(0)\neq 0,
\]
the local model may be normalized to
\[
Q_v(x)=(x^n,x,x^2),
\qquad n\ge 3,
\]
so that
\[
\ord_0 T_v=n-3.
\]
For the model, the exact four-point coplanarity determinant is the generalized
Vandermonde for exponents \(0,1,2,n\), hence
\[
\Delta_4^{\mathrm{model}}
=
\pm V_4\,h_{n-3},
\]
where \(h_{n-3}\) is the complete symmetric polynomial of degree \(n-3\).

The repeated-node tangent-plane contact determinant factors as
\[
\widetilde\Delta_n(a,u,v)
=
-(u-a)^2(v-a)^2(u-v)\,P_{n-3}(a,u,v),
\]
where \(P_{n-3}(a,u,v)=f[a,a,u,v]\) for \(f(x)=x^n\). Thus:
\begin{itemize}
\item if \(n\) is odd (equivalently \(\ord_0 T_v\) is even), there is no
opposite-side tangent-plane contact branch in the model;
\item if \(n\) is even (equivalently \(\ord_0 T_v\) is odd), the model carries a
unique opposite-side tangent-plane contact branch cone, and in the exact model
this persists as a unique local exact branch sheet on compact opposite-side
cones.
\end{itemize}

In particular, blanket local exclusion near nonmixed odd-order \(T_v\)-zeros is
false generically. The remaining issue on the nonmixed four-point side is not
local existence, but whether this unique local exact sheet can satisfy the extra
algebraic compatibility conditions imposed by a true bad four-point core.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Progress on the mixed lifted four-point branch]
\label{rem:progress-mixed-four-point-branch}
At a mixed lifted point
\[
K_v(0)=0,\qquad T_v(0)=0,
\]
the current analysis leads after affine normalization to the monomial model
\[
Q_v(x)\sim (x^n,x,x^m),
\qquad m\ge 3,\qquad n>m.
\]
If
\[
r:=\ord_0 K_v,
\qquad
s:=\ord_0 T_v,
\]
then the model exponents satisfy
\[
m=r+2,
\qquad
n=s-r+3.
\]
The leading four-point coplanarity determinant is the generalized Vandermonde
for exponents
\[
0,\ 1,\ m,\ n.
\]
In particular, the immediately dangerous mixed sector is
\[
n\ \text{even}
\qquad\Longleftrightarrow\qquad
s-r\ \text{odd}.
\]
The only universal order inequality visible in generic smooth models is
\[
s\ge 2r.
\]
Thus no generic parity obstruction is available; any exclusion of dangerous
mixed patterns must come from RH-specific jet identities or from extra algebraic
compatibility conditions beyond mere coplanarity.
\end{remark}

This captures the key formulas and progress without overclaiming closure.

\begin{remark}[Work in progress: what remains in the lifted order-$7$ geometry]
\label{rem:wip-lifted-order7-zero-capture}
The lifted \(v_5\)-patch geometry now splits more sharply than a blanket
zero-capture problem.

First, Propositions~\ref{prop:shrinking-exact-lifted-three-point-circuits}
and~\ref{prop:shrinking-exact-lifted-four-point-circuits} show that shrinking

Second, Lemmas~\ref{lem:repeated-node-tangent-line-bridge}
and~\ref{lem:repeated-node-tangent-plane-bridge} identify the one-pair
collapse limits as tangent-line and tangent-plane contact determinants for the
lifted curves \(\Lambda_v\) and \(Q_v\).

Third, the nonmixed and mixed four-point local pictures are genuinely different:
nonmixed odd-order \(T_v\)-zeros support a unique local exact branch sheet in
the generic model, whereas the mixed case \(K_v=T_v=0\) remains the true
codimension-two local obstruction.

Thus the missing global ingredient is no longer a single blanket first-contact
lemma. It is a combination of:
\begin{itemize}
\item source-level control of the multi-pair interaction defects
\[
E_{\ge2}^{(3)},\qquad E_{\ge2}^{(5)},\qquad \overline E_{\ge2}^{(7)};
\]
\item extra algebraic compatibility conditions for true bad four-point cores,
beyond generic coplanarity of the lifted points;
\item and, on the mixed side, RH-specific jet restrictions excluding the
dangerous exponent patterns.
\end{itemize}
\end{remark}

\begin{proposition}[Exact \(x\)-coordinate identities for the lifted \(4\)-point invariants]
\label{prop:exact-x-coordinate-identities-lifted-four-point}
On a good \(v_5\)-patch, write
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c},
\qquad
Y=\frac{u_5}{c},
\qquad
S=\sigma_v=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}.
\]
Then:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the lifted planar curvature numerator satisfies
\[
K_v=(x')^3\,S''(x);
\]
\item the lifted \(4\)-point Wronskian satisfies
\[
T_v=(x')^6\,W_x(1,Y,x,S)
=(x')^6\bigl(S''Y'''-S'''Y''\bigr);
\]
\item equivalently,
\[
T_v=(x')^6\,S''^{\,2}\,\frac{d}{dx}\!\left(\frac{Y''}{S''}\right)
=K_v^{\,2}\,\frac{d}{dx}\!\left(\frac{Y''}{S''}\right).
\]
\end{enumerate}
In particular, \(K_v\) and \(S''\) have the same zero set and the same
vanishing order on every good \(v_5\)-patch.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By definition,
\[
K_v=x'\sigma_v''-\sigma_v' x''.
\]
Since \(S=\sigma_v\) as a function of the local coordinate \(x\), we have
\[
\sigma_v'=S' x',
\qquad
\sigma_v''=S''(x')^2+S' x'',
\]
hence
\[
K_v=x'\bigl(S''(x')^2+S'x''\bigr)-S' x' x''=(x')^3S''.
\]

Next,
\[
T_v=W_h(1,Y,x,S).
\]
Under reparametrization \(h\mapsto x(h)\), a \(4\times4\) Wronskian gains the
factor \((x')^{0+1+2+3}=(x')^6\), so
\[
T_v=(x')^6\,W_x(1,Y,x,S).
\]
Now
\[
W_x(1,Y,x,S)
=
\det\!\begin{pmatrix}
1&Y&x&S\\
0&Y'&1&S'\\
0&Y''&0&S''\\
0&Y'''&0&S'''
\end{pmatrix}
=
S''Y'''-S'''Y'',
\]
which proves the second identity.

Finally,
\[
S''Y'''-S'''Y''
=
S''^{\,2}\,\frac{d}{dx}\!\left(\frac{Y''}{S''}\right),
\]
and using \(K_v=(x')^3S''\) gives
\[
(x')^6S''^{\,2}=K_v^{\,2}.
\]
This yields the third identity.
\end{proof}

This is the exact coordinate calculus you were using informally. It should be theorem-level.

\begin{remark}[Exact nonmixed jet reduction for the lifted \(4\)-point branch]
\label{rem:nonmixed-four-point-zeros-can-carry-preexisting-branches}
At a nonmixed lifted point
\[
K_v(0)\neq 0,
\qquad
T_v(0)=0,
\]

\[
T_v=(x')^6\,S''^{\,2}\,\frac{d}{dx}\!\left(\frac{Y''}{S''}\right).
\]
Since \(K_v(0)\neq 0\), one has \(S''(0)\neq 0\), so after analytic
reparametrization and affine target normalization preserving coplanarity one may

\[
Q_v(\xi)=\bigl(\widetilde Y(\xi),\,\xi,\,\xi^2\bigr),
\qquad
\widetilde Y(0)=\widetilde Y'(0)=\widetilde Y''(0)=0.
\]
In these normalized coordinates,
\[
W_\xi(1,\widetilde Y,\xi,\xi^2)=2\,\widetilde Y'''.
\]
Thus the nonmixed lifted \(4\)-point problem is exactly the jet problem of
excluding odd-order zeros of \(\widetilde Y'''\).

In particular, the low-order dangerous nonmixed cases are exactly:
\[
\operatorname{ord}_0 T_v=1
\iff
\widetilde Y'''(0)=0,\ \widetilde Y^{(4)}(0)\neq 0,
\]
\[
\operatorname{ord}_0 T_v=3
\iff
\widetilde Y^{(3)}(0)=\widetilde Y^{(4)}(0)=\widetilde Y^{(5)}(0)=0,\
\widetilde Y^{(6)}(0)\neq 0,
\]
\[
\operatorname{ord}_0 T_v=5
\iff
\widetilde Y^{(3)}(0)=\cdots=\widetilde Y^{(7)}(0)=0,\
\widetilde Y^{(8)}(0)\neq 0.
\]

So the nonmixed \(4\)-point endgame has been reduced to the finite jet problem:
rule out leading terms of \(\widetilde Y\) in degrees \(4,6,8\).

This is strictly sharper than the earlier qualitative statement that
nonmixed odd-order \(T_v\)-zeros can carry preexisting close branches.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Exact mixed jet reduction and low-order dangerous list]

\begin{proposition}[Realization lemma for lifted germs]
\label{prop:realization-lemma-lifted-germs}
Let \(\widetilde Y(\xi)\) and \(\widetilde S(\xi)\) be arbitrary analytic germs
at \(\xi=0\). Define
\[
c(\xi)\equiv 1,
\qquad
v_5(\xi):=1+\xi,
\qquad
u_5(\xi):=\widetilde Y(\xi),
\qquad
\Delta_7(\xi):=(1+\xi)\widetilde S(\xi).
\]
Then on a sufficiently small neighborhood of \(0\),
\[
c\neq 0,
\qquad
v_5\neq 0,
\qquad
M=c\,v_5'-c'v_5=1\neq 0,
\]
so this is a good \(v_5\)-patch. The normalized lifted coordinates are
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c}=1+\xi,
\qquad
Y=\frac{u_5}{c}=\widetilde Y(\xi),
\qquad
S=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}=\widetilde S(\xi).
\]
After the affine shift \(x\mapsto x-1\), the lifted germ becomes
\[
Q_v(\xi)=\bigl(\widetilde Y(\xi),\,\xi,\,\widetilde S(\xi)\bigr).
\]

Thus every analytic pair of germs \((\widetilde Y,\widetilde S)\) occurs, after
affine normalization, as the lifted pair \((Y,S)\) on some good \(v_5\)-patch.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The displayed formulas are immediate from the definitions. The hypotheses
\(c\neq 0\), \(v_5\neq 0\), and \(M=1\neq 0\) hold on a sufficiently small
neighborhood of \(0\), and the formulas for \(x,Y,S\) are direct.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[No new jet obstruction is available at the current lifted level]
\label{cor:no-new-jet-obstruction-current-lifted-level}
No identity involving only
\[
c,\qquad v_5,\qquad u_5,\qquad \Delta_7
\]
and their derivatives can exclude the low-order dangerous lifted \(4\)-point
patterns listed above.

In particular, the dangerous nonmixed models
\[
Q_v(\xi)=(\xi^n,\xi,\xi^2),
\qquad n=4,6,8,
\]
and the dangerous mixed models
\[
Q_v(\xi)=(\xi^n,\xi,\xi^m),
\qquad (m,n)=(3,4),\ (3,6),\ (4,6),
\]
are all realizable at the present lifted level.

Consequently, any RH-specific obstruction to these low-order \(4\)-point
patterns must use information not encoded in the current lifted variables
\[
(c,v_5,u_5,\Delta_7)
\]
alone. It must come from deeper source-level corrected quotient-germ structure,
matrix-level identities behind \((u_5,\Delta_7)\), or an additional symmetry
not yet visible in the present lifted formulation.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Apply Proposition~\ref{prop:realization-lemma-lifted-germs} with
\[
(\widetilde Y,\widetilde S)=(\xi^n,\xi^2)
\]
for the nonmixed cases, and with
\[
(\widetilde Y,\widetilde S)=(\xi^n,\xi^m)
\]
for the mixed cases.
\end{proof}

This is the single most important new “negative theorem” to add so you stop chasing impossible lifted-level identities.

Insert this LaTeX

\begin{proposition}[Canonical scalar invariants \(\mathcal Z\) and \(\mathcal R\) on a nonmixed lifted patch]
\label{prop:canonical-Z-R-invariants-lifted-four-point}
On a good \(v_5\)-patch, write
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c},
\qquad
Y=\frac{u_5}{c},
\qquad
S=\sigma_v=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}.
\]
On the nonmixed subregion where \(K_v\neq 0\), define
\[
\mathcal Z:=\frac{Y''}{S''},
\qquad
\mathcal R:=\frac{d\mathcal Z}{dx}.
\]
Then:
\begin{enumerate}
\item
\[
\mathcal R=\frac{T_v}{K_v^2};
\]
\item under the affine gauge
\[
Y\longmapsto Y+\alpha+\beta x+\gamma S,
\]
one has
\[
\mathcal Z\longmapsto \mathcal Z+\gamma,
\qquad
\mathcal R\longmapsto \mathcal R.
\]
Hence \(\mathcal R\) is the canonical scalar invariant of the lifted
\(4\)-point branch on every nonmixed patch.
\end{enumerate}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By Proposition~\ref{prop:exact-x-coordinate-identities-lifted-four-point},
\[
T_v=(x')^6\,S''^{\,2}\,\frac{d}{dx}\!\left(\frac{Y''}{S''}\right)
=K_v^{\,2}\,\frac{d}{dx}\!\left(\frac{Y''}{S''}\right),
\]
so
\[
\mathcal R=\frac{d}{dx}\!\left(\frac{Y''}{S''}\right)=\frac{T_v}{K_v^2}.
\]

For the gauge transformation, one has
\[
(Y+\alpha+\beta x+\gamma S)''=Y''+\gamma S'',
\]
hence
\[
\mathcal Z\longmapsto \frac{Y''+\gamma S''}{S''}=\mathcal Z+\gamma.
\]
Differentiating with respect to \(x\) gives \(\mathcal R\mapsto \mathcal R\).
\end{proof}

Yes. Here is the actual groundwork you can use.

The right move is to work in the **centered symmetric-placement variable**
\[
t_\pm=h\pm \frac{s}{2},
\]
and treat \(s\mapsto -s\) as swapping the two microscopic points. Then every \(2\times 2\) symmetric coefficient matrix
\[
X_n(s)=\begin{pmatrix}a_n(s)&b_n(s)\\ b_n(s)&c_n(s)\end{pmatrix}
\]
satisfies
\[
a_n(-s)=c_n(s),\qquad b_n(-s)=b_n(s),\qquad c_n(-s)=a_n(s).
\]

So define the even/odd half-sum/half-difference variables
\[
\bar a_n:=\frac{a_n+c_n}{2}\quad\text{(even)},\qquad
\delta a_n:=\frac{c_n-a_n}{2}\quad\text{(odd)},
\]
and similarly for every diagonal pair, while the off-diagonal entry is always even.

Concretely, for the matrices already in the paper:
\[
X_1=\begin{pmatrix}u&v\\v&w\end{pmatrix},\quad
X_2=\begin{pmatrix}a&b\\b&c\end{pmatrix},\quad
X_4=\begin{pmatrix}p&r\\r&s\end{pmatrix},
\]
\[
X_5=\begin{pmatrix}\alpha_5&\beta_5\\ \beta_5&\gamma_5\end{pmatrix},\quad
X_6=\begin{pmatrix}\mu_6&\nu_6\\ \nu_6&\lambda_6\end{pmatrix},
\]
set
\[
\bar u=\frac{u+w}{2},\quad \delta u=\frac{u-w}{2},\qquad
\bar a=\frac{a+c}{2},\quad \delta a=\frac{c-a}{2},
\]
\[
\bar p=\frac{p+s}{2},\quad \delta p=\frac{p-s}{2},\qquad
\bar\alpha_5=\frac{\alpha_5+\gamma_5}{2},\quad \delta\alpha_5=\frac{\gamma_5-\alpha_5}{2},
\]
\[
\bar\mu_6=\frac{\mu_6+\lambda_6}{2},\quad \delta\mu_6=\frac{\lambda_6-\mu_6}{2},
\]
and for the baseline diagonal block
\[
X_0=\diag(x_1,x_2),\qquad
\bar x=\frac{x_1+x_2}{2},\quad \delta x=\frac{x_2-x_1}{2}.
\]

Then the parity is:

- even:
\[
\bar x,\ \bar u,\ v,\ \bar a,\ b,\ \bar p,\ r,\ \bar\alpha_5,\ \beta_5,\ \bar\mu_6,\ \nu_6
\]
- odd:
\[
\delta x,\ \delta u,\ \delta a,\ \delta p,\ \delta\alpha_5,\ \delta\mu_6.
\]

That much is formal from centered symmetric placement.

Now rewrite the canonical quintic and septic transport formulas in these variables.

## 1. Quintic fixed-sector package

From the file,
\[
u_5^{(\mathrm{comm})}=v(\gamma-\alpha)+\beta(u-w),
\qquad
v_5^{(\mathrm{comm})}=\gamma u-\alpha w.
\]

Using
\[
\gamma-\alpha=2\,\delta\alpha,\qquad
u-w=2\,\delta u,
\]
and
\[
\gamma u-\alpha w
=
2(\bar\alpha\,\delta u+\delta\alpha\,\bar u),
\]
you get
\[
\boxed{
u_5=2\bigl(v\,\delta\alpha+\beta\,\delta u\bigr),
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
v_5=2\bigl(\bar\alpha\,\delta u+\delta\alpha\,\bar u\bigr).
}
\]

So both \(u_5\) and \(v_5\) are **odd functions of \(s\)**.

This is the first real Taylor groundwork fact.

Write the even variables as
\[
E(s)=E_0+E_2 s^2+E_4 s^4+E_6 s^6+\cdots
\]
and the odd variables as
\[
O(s)=O_1 s+O_3 s^3+O_5 s^5+O_7 s^7+\cdots.
\]

Then
\[
u_5(s)=U_1 s+U_3 s^3+U_5 s^5+U_7 s^7+\cdots
\]
with
\[
\boxed{
U_1=2\bigl(v_0\,\delta\alpha_1+\beta_0\,\delta u_1\bigr),
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
U_3=2\bigl(v_0\,\delta\alpha_3+v_2\,\delta\alpha_1+\beta_0\,\delta u_3+\beta_2\,\delta u_1\bigr),
}
\]
and similarly
\[
\boxed{
U_5=2\bigl(v_0\,\delta\alpha_5+v_2\,\delta\alpha_3+v_4\,\delta\alpha_1+\beta_0\,\delta u_5+\beta_2\,\delta u_3+\beta_4\,\delta u_1\bigr).
}
\]

Likewise
\[
v_5(s)=V_1 s+V_3 s^3+V_5 s^5+V_7 s^7+\cdots
\]
with
\[
\boxed{
V_1=2\bigl(\bar\alpha_0\,\delta u_1+\delta\alpha_1\,\bar u_0\bigr),
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
V_3=2\bigl(\bar\alpha_0\,\delta u_3+\bar\alpha_2\,\delta u_1+\delta\alpha_1\,\bar u_2+\delta\alpha_3\,\bar u_0\bigr),
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
V_5=2\bigl(\bar\alpha_0\,\delta u_5+\bar\alpha_2\,\delta u_3+\bar\alpha_4\,\delta u_1+\delta\alpha_1\,\bar u_4+\delta\alpha_3\,\bar u_2+\delta\alpha_5\,\bar u_0\bigr).
}
\]

So the quintic canonical package has a fully explicit **odd Taylor expansion** in centered \(s\).

## 2. Septic \(K_1\)-transport package

From the exact formulas in the file,
\[
u_{7,K_1}
=
\kappa\Bigl(

+

Rewrite each term.

Since
\[
x_2-x_1=2\delta x,\quad
u-w=2\delta u,\quad
\gamma_5-\alpha_5=2\delta\alpha_5,\quad
p-s=2\delta p,\quad

you get
\[

u_{7,K_1}
=
2\kappa\bigl(

\bigr).
}
\]

For the \(S\)-component, use
\[
x_2\mu_6-x_1\lambda_6
=

\[

\[

=

+\bar a\,\delta p+\delta a\,\bar p
\bigr).
}
\]

Therefore \(u_{7,K_1}\) and \(v_{7,K_1}\) are also **odd functions of \(s\)**.

Write
\[
u_{7,K_1}(s)=\widehat U_1 s+\widehat U_3 s^3+\widehat U_5 s^5+\cdots,
\qquad

\[

=
2\kappa\bigl(

+r_0\,\delta a_1

## 3. The determinant \(\Delta_7\)

Since the current file proves
\[

\]

These are the actual Taylor coefficients you asked to get to.
