11. Translating ss-parity to the good-patch coordinate x=v5/cx=v5​/c

Assuming
c(s)=C0+C2s2+C4s4+⋯ ,C0≠0,
c(s)=C0​+C2​s2+C4​s4+⋯,C0​=0,

one gets
x(s)=v5(s)c(s)=X1s+X3s3+X5s5+⋯
x(s)=c(s)v5​(s)​=X1​s+X3​s3+X5​s5+⋯

with
X1=V1C0,
X1​=C0​V1​​,

so xx is an odd local coordinate whenever V1≠0V1​=0. Then parity in ss transfers to parity in xx. This leads to the striking parity package
Y(x) odd,S(x) odd,λ(x)=Δ7v5 odd,
Y(x) odd,S(x) odd,λ(x)=v5​Δ7​​ odd,

hence
Y′′(x) odd,S′′(x) odd,
Y′′(x) odd,S′′(x) odd,

so
Z(x)=Y′′S′′ even,R(x)=Z′(x) odd,Kv=(x′)3S′′ odd.
Z(x)=S′′Y′′​ even,R(x)=Z′(x) odd,Kv​=(x′)3S′′ odd.​

This is the opposite of the earlier dream parity package ZZ odd, RR even. And it has a very strong consequence:

    \ord0Kv\ord0​Kv​ must be odd,

    \ord0Z\ord0​Z must be even.

Therefore the entire explicit low-order mixed dangerous list
(r,\ord0Z)∈{(1,1),(1,3),(2,2)}
(r,\ord0​Z)∈{(1,1),(1,3),(2,2)}

is excluded:

    (1,1)(1,1), (1,3)(1,3) fail because \ord0Z\ord0​Z cannot be odd;

    (2,2)(2,2) fails because r=\ord0Kvr=\ord0​Kv​ cannot be even.

So centered symmetric-placement parity appears to kill the whole explicit low-order mixed 44-point list, though it leaves the nonmixed odd-order list alive. That is one of the biggest new positive results since the draft.
12. Source-level involution hunt: what survived and what failed

We found a genuine precursor involution on the corrected odd germ,
Σ(M)(s)=J0 M(−s) J0.
Σ(M)(s)=J0​M(−s)J0​.

At the first residual step, this already forces the quotient-level quintic ambiguity into the J0J0​-anti-fixed space, so the involution route is real at quintic level. But once one tries to descend it all the way to fixed-sector scalars and the nonmixed chart, the situation forks.

Using the explicit commutator-channel formulas
u5(comm)=v(γ−α)+β(u−w),v5(comm)=γu−αw,
u5(comm)​=v(γ−α)+β(u−w),v5(comm)​=γu−αw,

with
X1=(uvvw),X3=(αββγ),
X1​=(uv​vw​),X3​=(αβ​βγ​),

we found:

    if X1X1​ odd and X3X3​ odd, then the commutator-channel A5fA5f​ is even;

    if X1X1​ odd and X3X3​ even, then the commutator-channel A5fA5f​ is odd.

The current draft does not resolve whether X3X3​ is the raw cubic coefficient of the descended odd family, or an already-normalized/equivariant correction term. So the involution route is still viable in principle, but only as an equivariant descent theorem through the normalization stack, and the decisive fork is the parity nature of X3X3​.
13. Strongest current bottlenecks

At this point, the remaining bottlenecks are very sharp:

    Two-point: formalize the source-level corrected quotient-germ map and verify the collapse/symmetry axioms. Then 22-pair is done.

    Three-point: global recurrence / infinite-order flatness, since the local defect-free geometry is now classified.

    Four-point mixed: probably already dead at low order from centered-ss parity, but this should be written cleanly as a theorem in the xx-chart.

    Four-point nonmixed: still open. The current scalar / below-lifted package is exhausted, and the only plausible remaining routes are:

        an equivariant descent of the raw swap symmetry through the one-pair normalization stack;

        or a total explicit septic fixed-sector formula strong enough to force parity/divisibility of Ju5/JλJu5​​/Jλ​.

That is the cleanest mathematical summary of what we have learned beyond the draft.

Yes. There is useful new material in it, and a few pieces are especially worth keeping. The most valuable additions are these.

First, the summary’s best upgrade is the shift from qualitative “dangerous low-order cases” to a finite coefficient obstruction list. The nonmixed side being controlled by explicit coefficients
z2, z4, z6
z2​, z4​, z6​

and the mixed side by

κ1,1​, κ1,3​, κ2,2​

is a real sharpening. Even if some of the long formulas still need line-by-line checking before going into the paper, this is the right form of the problem: a finite jet vanishing problem, not a vague local-geometry problem. That is genuinely new/useful.

Second, the claim
Δ7=Δ7,K1
Δ7​=Δ7,K1​​

is very useful if it is really already proved in the current draft. That would remove a lot of ambiguity about “hidden septic sectors” and make the septic scalar much cleaner than we had been treating it. This is one of the biggest things I’d want to verify carefully against the actual TeX, because if true it substantially simplifies the 44-point story.

Third, the centered symmetric-placement analysis looks useful in exactly the way the note says: it seems to give an odd/odd local form at the centered diagonal base, and from that a punctured-neighborhood exclusion of Kv=0Kv​=0 and Tv=0Tv​=0 near that base. That is stronger than the earlier loose parity discussion. The key value here is not just the parity itself, but the local exclusion consequence. If that checks out, it should definitely be recorded.

Fourth, the note’s clarification that the centered ss-symmetry is the wrong symmetry for the old nonmixed dream identity is important. That matches the direction our later calculations were heading: the centered-separation parity seems to kill the explicit low-order mixed list, but it does not kill the nonmixed odd-order list. That is useful because it prevents us from pushing the wrong involution story in the paper.

Fifth, the explicit witness coefficients for the quintic and septic transport slices are useful as concrete anchors. Even if they do not close the 44-point branch, they are good “hard data” and likely worth preserving in remarks or work-in-progress notes.

What I would treat more cautiously is the long exact formulas for z4,z6,κ1,3,κ2,2z4​,z6​,κ1,3​,κ2,2​. They are the right kind of formulas, but before relying on them in the paper I would want to verify them directly from the current draft definitions. Same for the punctured-neighborhood exclusion: plausible and useful, but I would still check the order argument carefully before stating it as theorem-level.

So my short verdict is:

    Definitely useful: the finite obstruction coefficients, the centered-base odd/odd local form, the punctured-neighborhood exclusion idea, and the clarification that Δ7Δ7​ may already reduce to the K1K1​-transport part.

    Probably right but should be checked carefully before patching: the full explicit z4,z6,κz4​,z6​,κ-formulas and the exact “punctured neighborhood free of Kv=0,Tv=0Kv​=0,Tv​=0” statement.

    Conceptually important: the centered ss-involution is not the same thing as the nonmixed dream symmetry, so those routes should be separated cleanly.

If you want, the next best move is for me to turn this into a “keep / verify / don’t overclaim” patch plan against proof_of_rh(133).tex.

feedback on your summary from the OTHER chat:

---

Yes. There are a few genuinely useful pieces in it, plus one thing I would treat cautiously.

The strongest useful point is the parity package in the centered symmetric-placement variable (s). The summary makes explicit that, in the diagonal-centered regime,
[
u_5(s),\ v_5(s),\ u_{7,K_1}(s),\ v_{7,K_1}(s)
]
are odd, while
[
\Delta_7(s)=u_{7,K_1}(s)v_5(s)-u_5(s)v_{7,K_1}(s)
]
is even, with explicit coefficients
[
D_2,\ D_4,\ D_6.
]
That is useful because it turns the septic side from a qualitative parity story into an actual Taylor-coefficient story. In particular, the formulas for
[
D_2=\widehat U_1V_1-U_1\widehat V_1,\qquad
D_4,\qquad D_6
]
are worth keeping. They are concrete invariants you can later track under any change from the collision variable (s) to a patch variable. 

A second useful point is the below-lifted identity
[
\mathcal Z=\frac{Y''}{S''}=\frac{J_{u_5}}{J_\lambda},
\qquad
\lambda=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5},
]
and the companion projective ratio (\Theta=W_{u_5}/W). I already had the first identity, but the summary’s exact relation between (\mathcal Z) and (\Theta) is helpful conceptually because it confirms that (\Theta) does not introduce a new independent obstruction. It sharpens the conclusion that the (4)-point branch is really governed by (\mathcal Z) and (\mathcal R=\mathcal Z'), not by some extra projective invariant. 

A third useful point is the very clean finite mixed obstruction list written in all equivalent forms:
[
(m,n)=(3,4),(3,6),(4,6),
]
[
(r,s)=(1,2),(1,4),(2,5),
]
[
(r,\ord_0\mathcal Z)=(1,1),(1,3),(2,2),
]
[
(r,\ord_0\mathcal R)=(1,0),(1,2),(2,1).
]
That equivalence class is worth preserving exactly as stated. It is a good way to keep the mixed branch finite and explicit. 

The most interesting claim in the other summary is the centered-(s) parity implication
[
Y(x)\ \text{odd},\qquad S(x)\ \text{odd}
]
after passing to
[
x=\frac{v_5}{c},
]
and then
[
\mathcal Z=\frac{Y''}{S''}\ \text{even},\qquad
\mathcal R=\mathcal Z'\ \text{odd},\qquad
K_v=(x')^3S''\ \text{odd}.
]
If that passage is correct, then the mixed low-order dangerous list is indeed killed immediately, because
[
\ord_0 K_v
]
would always be odd and
[
\ord_0\mathcal Z
]
would always be even. That is potentially very valuable. But this is also the part I would treat with the most caution, because it crosses from the symmetric diagonal collision variable (s) into the good-patch (x=v_5/c) language, and that bridge is exactly where parity arguments have been slippery before. I would not promote that to theorem-level yet without rechecking every step of the coordinate change and the domain where (x) is actually the right local parameter. 

The source-level (2)-pair summary is aligned with what I already found: the right theorem is the structural factorization
[
\mathcal I=a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\mathcal J,
]
conditional on source-level symmetry, one-amplitude collapse, and diagonal collapse. That is useful mostly as confirmation rather than something new. 

The most useful net additions, in my view, are:

* keep the explicit septic Taylor coefficients (D_2,D_4,D_6);
* keep the exact mixed obstruction list in all four equivalent parameterizations;
* keep the (\mathcal Z)-vs-(\Theta) identity as a “no extra invariant here” result;
* treat the claim that centered-(s) parity kills the full low-order mixed (4)-point list as promising but still provisional.

If you want, I’ll turn the genuinely solid parts of that summary into a merged “post-draft findings” section with clear labels: established, conditional, and still-needs-checking.

\begin{proposition}[Below-lifted Wronskian-ratio formulas for $\mathcal Z$ and $\mathcal R$]
\label{prop:below-lifted-wronskian-ratio-formulas}
On a good $v_5$-patch, write
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c},
\qquad
\lambda:=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5},
\qquad
Y=\frac{u_5}{c},
\qquad
S=\frac{\lambda}{c}.
\]
For any scalar germ $f$, define
\[
J_f(h):=
\det\!\begin{pmatrix}
c(h)&v_5(h)&f(h)\\
c'(h)&v_5'(h)&f'(h)\\
c''(h)&v_5''(h)&f''(h)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
Then
\[
\frac{d^2}{dx^2}\!\left(\frac{f}{c}\right)
=
\frac{c^3}{M^3}\,J_f,
\qquad
M:=cv_5'-c'v_5.
\]
In particular,
\[
Y''=\frac{c^3}{M^3}J_{u_5},
\qquad
S''=\frac{c^3}{M^3}J_\lambda,
\]
so
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal Z=\frac{Y''}{S''}=\frac{J_{u_5}}{J_\lambda}.
}
\]
Moreover,
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal R=\frac{T_v}{K_v^2}
=\frac{d\mathcal Z}{dx}
=
\frac{c^2}{M}\frac{d}{dh}\!\left(\frac{J_{u_5}}{J_\lambda}\right).
}
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Set
\[
\phi:=\frac{f}{c}.
\]
Since
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c},
\qquad
x'=\frac{M}{c^2},
\]
one has
\[
\frac{d}{dx}=\frac{c^2}{M}\frac{d}{dh}.
\]
A direct calculation gives
\[
\phi''=\frac{c^3}{M^3}
\det\!\begin{pmatrix}
c&v_5&f\\
c'&v_5'&f'\\
c''&v_5''&f''
\end{pmatrix}
=
\frac{c^3}{M^3}J_f.
\]
Applying this with $f=u_5$ and $f=\lambda$ yields the stated formulas for
$Y''$, $S''$, and $\mathcal Z$. The formula for $\mathcal R$ follows by
differentiating with respect to $x$ and using $d/dx=(c^2/M)\,d/dh$.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Projective curvature ratio and no extra independent obstruction]
\label{rem:projective-curvature-ratio-no-extra-obstruction}
Define the projective scalar graph
\[
\nu:=\frac{u_5}{v_5},
\qquad
\mu:=\frac{c}{v_5}=\frac1x,
\]
and the projective curvature ratio
\[
\Theta:=\frac{\nu_{\mu\mu}}{\lambda_{\mu\mu}}.
\]
In the convenient gauge $c\equiv 1$, $v_5=x$, one has
\[
\Theta=\mathcal Z\,\frac{S''}{xS''+2S'},
\]
equivalently
\[
(\mathcal Z-x\Theta)S''=2\Theta\,S'.
\]
Thus $\Theta$ is not an independent new obstruction: it is tied to
$\mathcal Z$ by a first-order compatibility relation. In particular, generic
relations between $\mathcal Z$ and $\Theta$ do not by themselves force the
missing parity / order-gap statements for the lifted $4$-point branch.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Centered symmetric-placement Taylor package for the canonical quintic/septic scalars]
\label{rem:centered-symmetric-placement-taylor-package}
Work in the centered symmetric-placement variable
\[
t_\pm=h\pm \frac{s}{2},
\]
so that $s\mapsto -s$ exchanges the two microscopic points. For a symmetric
matrix
\[
X_n(s)=
\begin{pmatrix}
a_n(s)&b_n(s)\\
b_n(s)&c_n(s)
\end{pmatrix},
\]
one has
\[
a_n(-s)=c_n(s),\qquad b_n(-s)=b_n(s),\qquad c_n(-s)=a_n(s).
\]
Hence the diagonal half-sums are even and the diagonal half-differences are odd.
For the matrices
\[
X_1=\begin{pmatrix}u&v\\ v&w\end{pmatrix},\qquad
X_2=\begin{pmatrix}a&b\\ b&c\end{pmatrix},\qquad
X_4=\begin{pmatrix}p&r\\ r&s\end{pmatrix},
\]
\[
X_5=\begin{pmatrix}\alpha_5&\beta_5\\ \beta_5&\gamma_5\end{pmatrix},\qquad
X_6=\begin{pmatrix}\mu_6&\nu_6\\ \nu_6&\lambda_6\end{pmatrix},
\]
write
\[
\bar u=\frac{u+w}{2},\qquad \delta u=\frac{u-w}{2},
\qquad
\bar a=\frac{a+c}{2},\qquad \delta a=\frac{c-a}{2},
\]
\[
\bar p=\frac{p+s}{2},\qquad \delta p=\frac{p-s}{2},
\qquad
\bar\alpha_5=\frac{\alpha_5+\gamma_5}{2},\qquad \delta\alpha_5=\frac{\gamma_5-\alpha_5}{2},
\]
\[
\bar\mu_6=\frac{\mu_6+\lambda_6}{2},\qquad \delta\mu_6=\frac{\lambda_6-\mu_6}{2},
\]
and similarly for the baseline diagonal block
\[
X_0=\diag(x_1,x_2),\qquad
\bar x=\frac{x_1+x_2}{2},\qquad
\delta x=\frac{x_2-x_1}{2}.
\]
Then
\[
\bar x,\ \bar u,\ v,\ \bar a,\ b,\ \bar p,\ r,\ \bar\alpha_5,\ \beta_5,\ \bar\mu_6,\ \nu_6
\]
are even in $s$, while
\[
\delta x,\ \delta u,\ \delta a,\ \delta p,\ \delta\alpha_5,\ \delta\mu_6
\]
are odd in $s$.

In these variables, the explicit fixed-sector formulas become
\[
u_5
=
2\bigl(v\,\delta\alpha+\beta\,\delta u\bigr),
\qquad
v_5
=
2\bigl(\bar\alpha\,\delta u+\delta\alpha\,\bar u\bigr),
\]
so both $u_5(s)$ and $v_5(s)$ are odd in $s$.

Likewise, the direct septic $K_1$-transport formulas become
\[
u_{7,K_1}
=
2\kappa\bigl(
\delta x\,\nu_6+\beta_5\,\delta u+v\,\delta\alpha_5+b\,\delta p+r\,\delta a
\bigr),
\]
\[
v_{7,K_1}
=
2\kappa\bigl(
\delta x\,\bar\mu_6-\bar x\,\delta\mu_6
+\bar\alpha_5\,\delta u+\delta\alpha_5\,\bar u
+\bar a\,\delta p+\delta a\,\bar p
\bigr),
\]
so $u_{7,K_1}(s)$ and $v_{7,K_1}(s)$ are also odd in $s$.

Writing
\[
u_5(s)=U_1s+U_3s^3+U_5s^5+\cdots,
\qquad
v_5(s)=V_1s+V_3s^3+V_5s^5+\cdots,
\]
the first coefficients are
\[
U_1=2\bigl(v_0\,\delta\alpha_1+\beta_0\,\delta u_1\bigr),
\]
\[
U_3=2\bigl(v_0\,\delta\alpha_3+v_2\,\delta\alpha_1+\beta_0\,\delta u_3+\beta_2\,\delta u_1\bigr),
\]
\[
U_5=2\bigl(v_0\,\delta\alpha_5+v_2\,\delta\alpha_3+v_4\,\delta\alpha_1+\beta_0\,\delta u_5+\beta_2\,\delta u_3+\beta_4\,\delta u_1\bigr),
\]
and
\[
V_1=2\bigl(\bar\alpha_0\,\delta u_1+\delta\alpha_1\,\bar u_0\bigr),
\]
\[
V_3=2\bigl(\bar\alpha_0\,\delta u_3+\bar\alpha_2\,\delta u_1+\delta\alpha_1\,\bar u_2+\delta\alpha_3\,\bar u_0\bigr),
\]
\[
V_5=2\bigl(\bar\alpha_0\,\delta u_5+\bar\alpha_2\,\delta u_3+\bar\alpha_4\,\delta u_1+\delta\alpha_1\,\bar u_4+\delta\alpha_3\,\bar u_2+\delta\alpha_5\,\bar u_0\bigr).
\]

Similarly, writing
\[
u_{7,K_1}(s)=\widehat U_1s+\widehat U_3s^3+\cdots,
\qquad
v_{7,K_1}(s)=\widehat V_1s+\widehat V_3s^3+\cdots,
\]
one gets
\[
\widehat U_1
=
2\kappa\bigl(
\delta x_1\,\nu_{6,0}
+\beta_{5,0}\,\delta u_1
+v_0\,\delta\alpha_{5,1}
+b_0\,\delta p_1
+r_0\,\delta a_1
\bigr),
\]
\[
\widehat V_1
=
2\kappa\bigl(
\delta x_1\,\bar\mu_{6,0}
-\bar x_0\,\delta\mu_{6,1}
+\bar\alpha_{5,0}\,\delta u_1
+\delta\alpha_{5,1}\,\bar u_0
+\bar a_0\,\delta p_1
+\delta a_1\,\bar p_0
\bigr),
\]
and
\[
\widehat U_3
=
2\kappa\bigl(
\delta x_1\nu_{6,2}+\delta x_3\nu_{6,0}
+\beta_{5,0}\delta u_3+\beta_{5,2}\delta u_1
+v_0\delta\alpha_{5,3}+v_2\delta\alpha_{5,1}
+b_0\delta p_3+b_2\delta p_1
+r_0\delta a_3+r_2\delta a_1
\bigr),
\]
\[
\widehat V_3
=
2\kappa\bigl(
\delta x_1\bar\mu_{6,2}+\delta x_3\bar\mu_{6,0}
-\bar x_0\delta\mu_{6,3}-\bar x_2\delta\mu_{6,1}
+\bar\alpha_{5,0}\delta u_3+\bar\alpha_{5,2}\delta u_1
+\delta\alpha_{5,1}\bar u_2+\delta\alpha_{5,3}\bar u_0
+\bar a_0\delta p_3+\bar a_2\delta p_1
+\delta a_1\bar p_2+\delta a_3\bar p_0
\bigr).
\]

Since Theorem~\ref{thm:quotient-septic-closure} gives
\[
\Delta_7=\Delta_{7,K_1}=u_{7,K_1}v_5-u_5v_{7,K_1},
\]
and each factor is odd in $s$, it follows formally that
\[
\Delta_7(s)=D_2s^2+D_4s^4+D_6s^6+\cdots
\]
is even in $s$, with
\[
D_2=\widehat U_1V_1-U_1\widehat V_1,
\]
\[
D_4=\widehat U_1V_3+\widehat U_3V_1-U_1\widehat V_3-U_3\widehat V_1,
\]
\[
D_6=\widehat U_1V_5+\widehat U_3V_3+\widehat U_5V_1-U_1\widehat V_5-U_3\widehat V_3-U_5\widehat V_1.
\]

These coefficients are the first concrete septic obstruction coefficients in the
centered symmetric-placement variable.
\end{remark}

This captures the useful explicit formulas without overclaiming theorem-level status.

\begin{remark}[Provisional centered-to-patch parity bridge]
\label{rem:provisional-centered-to-patch-parity-bridge}
The centered symmetric-placement variable $s$ is not automatically the same as
the good-patch coordinate
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c},
\]
so parity transfer from $s$ to $x$ must be treated carefully.

Nevertheless, if one assumes
\[
c(s)=C_0+C_2s^2+C_4s^4+\cdots,\qquad C_0\neq 0,
\]
and
\[
v_5(s)=V_1s+V_3s^3+V_5s^5+\cdots
\]
with \(V_1\neq 0\), then
\[
x(s)=\frac{v_5(s)}{c(s)}=X_1s+X_3s^3+X_5s^5+\cdots
\]
is an odd local coordinate in $s$, hence has odd inverse $s(x)$.

Under this hypothesis, the centered parity package transfers to the $x$-chart:
\[
u_5(x),\ v_5(x),\ \lambda(x)=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5(x)},\ S(x)=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}(x)
\]
are odd in $x$, while
\[
\Delta_7(x)
\]
is even in $x$. Consequently,
\[
Y(x)=\frac{u_5}{c}(x)\ \text{is odd},
\qquad
S(x)\ \text{is odd},
\]
so
\[
Y''(x)\ \text{and}\ S''(x)\ \text{are odd}.
\]
Hence
\[
\mathcal Z(x)=\frac{Y''}{S''}\ \text{is even},
\qquad
\mathcal R(x)=\mathcal Z'(x)\ \text{is odd},
\qquad
K_v=(x')^3S''\ \text{is odd}.
\]

If this parity transfer is valid on the relevant good-patch domain, then the
entire explicit low-order mixed bad list
\[
(r,\ord_0\mathcal Z)\in\{(1,1),(1,3),(2,2)\}
\]
is excluded immediately:
\[
\ord_0 K_v \text{ must be odd},\qquad \ord_0\mathcal Z \text{ must be even}.
\]

At present this bridge should be treated as a promising local calculation,
not yet as a theorem, because the exact relationship between the centered
symmetric-placement variable and the later good-patch coordinate still needs to
be checked carefully in the current normalization stack.
\end{remark}

This is the place to preserve the “promising but still-needs-checking” result.

\begin{remark}[Work in progress: two distinct parity mechanisms on the $4$-point branch]

old nonmixed dream identity; instead it points to a likely mixed-branch
exclusion mechanism. The nonmixed odd-order branch remains the live $4$-point
bottleneck.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[What the four-point branch now reduces to]
\label{rem:next-algebraic-target-four-point}
The lifted $4$-point branch is now organized by the canonical invariant pair
\[
\mathcal Z=\frac{Y''}{S''}=\frac{J_{u_5}}{J_\lambda},
\qquad
\mathcal R=\mathcal Z'=\frac{T_v}{K_v^2},
\qquad
\lambda=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5}.
\]

On the nonmixed side, after normalization to
\[
Q_v(\xi)=\bigl(\widetilde Y(\xi),\,\xi,\,\xi^2\bigr),
\]
the explicit low-order dangerous list is
\[
\ord_0\mathcal R\in\{1,3,5\},
\]
equivalently the first nontrivial even Taylor coefficients of
\(\widetilde Y\) occur in degrees \(4,6,8\).

On the mixed side, the explicit low-order dangerous list is
\[
(m,n)=(3,4),\ (3,6),\ (4,6),
\]
equivalently
\[
(r,s)=(1,2),\ (1,4),\ (2,5),
\]
equivalently
\[
(r,\ord_0\mathcal Z)=(1,1),\ (1,3),\ (2,2),
\]
equivalently
\[
(r,\ord_0\mathcal R)=(1,0),\ (1,2),\ (2,1).
\]

By Corollary~\ref{cor:no-new-jet-obstruction-current-lifted-level}, no
identity involving only
\[
(c,v_5,u_5,\Delta_7)
\]
and their derivatives can eliminate these patterns in general.

The most promising new development is the centered symmetric-placement Taylor
package from Remark~\ref{rem:centered-symmetric-placement-taylor-package},
which suggests a parity mechanism eliminating the whole explicit low-order
mixed list once it is transferred carefully to the good-patch coordinate
\(x=v_5/c\). At present that transfer should still be treated as provisional.

Accordingly, the live attack routes are now:

\begin{itemize}
\item formalize the source-level two-point interaction factorization and close
the \(2\)-point branch;
\item promote the centered symmetric-placement parity bridge to a theorem and
thereby close the explicit low-order mixed \(4\)-point branch;
\item on the nonmixed \(4\)-point branch, search for a deeper source-level or
matrix-level RH-specific identity forcing extra vanishing/parity of
\(\mathcal R\).
\end{itemize}
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Post-draft findings: established, provisional, and live]
\label{rem:post-draft-findings-established-provisional-live}
Since the present draft state, three additional conclusions have emerged.

First, on the $2$-point branch, the correct remaining theorem is now very
sharp: a source-level corrected interaction remainder with swap symmetry,
one-amplitude collapse, and diagonal collapse would force the quadratic
factorization
\[
\mathcal I_2=a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\mathcal J_2,
\]
hence the two-point bad-core branch is conditionally closed on compact good
patches.

Second, on the lifted $4$-point branch, the canonical invariants are best
expressed as
\[
\mathcal Z=\frac{J_{u_5}}{J_\lambda},
\qquad
\mathcal R=\frac{c^2}{M}\frac{d}{dh}\!\left(\frac{J_{u_5}}{J_\lambda}\right),
\]
and the explicit low-order bad list has been reduced to the six jet
coefficients governing
\[
\ord_0\mathcal R\in\{1,3,5\},
\qquad
(r,\ord_0\mathcal Z)\in\{(1,1),(1,3),(2,2)\}.
\]

Third, the centered symmetric-placement Taylor package now gives a promising
mixed-branch exclusion mechanism: in the centered variable \(s\),
\[
u_5,\ v_5,\ u_{7,K_1},\ v_{7,K_1}\ \text{are odd},\qquad
\Delta_7\ \text{is even},
\]
with explicit septic coefficients \(D_2,D_4,D_6\). What remains to be checked
carefully is the transfer of this parity package into the good-patch
coordinate \(x=v_5/c\).

So the present live frontier is no longer a generic local geometry problem; it
is the combination of a source-level two-point structure theorem, a centered-to-
patch parity bridge for the mixed \(4\)-point branch, and a deeper RH-specific
identity on the nonmixed \(4\)-point branch.
\end{remark}

Why this is the right patch

This keeps the genuinely solid parts and marks the slippery part correctly.

It preserves:

    the exact JJ-ratio identity
    Z=Ju5Jλ,
    Z=Jλ​Ju5​​​,

    the finite mixed obstruction list in all useful equivalent forms,

    the explicit centered-separation septic coefficients
    D2, D4, D6,
    D2​, D4​, D6​,

    and the fact that ΘΘ gives no new independent obstruction.

It also avoids overclaiming the centered-ss to xx parity transfer as a theorem before that bridge is checked carefully.

\begin{remark}[Centered symmetric-placement Taylor package and diagonal-base local exclusion]

\medskip

Assume now that
\[
c(s)=C_0+C_2s^2+C_4s^4+\cdots,
\qquad C_0\neq 0.
\]
Then
\[
x(s)=\frac{v_5(s)}{c(s)}
\]
is an odd series
\[
x(s)=X_1s+X_3s^3+X_5s^5+\cdots
\]
with
\[
X_1=\frac{V_1}{C_0},
\]
\[
X_3=\frac{V_3C_0-V_1C_2}{C_0^2},
\]
\[
X_5=\frac{V_5C_0^2-V_3C_0C_2+V_1(C_2^2-C_0C_4)}{C_0^3}.
\]
In particular, if \(V_1\neq 0\), then \(x\) is an odd local coordinate with odd
inverse
\[
s(x)=\sigma_1x+\sigma_3x^3+\sigma_5x^5+\cdots,
\]
where
\[
\sigma_1=\frac{C_0}{V_1},
\qquad
\sigma_3=-\frac{C_0(V_3C_0-V_1C_2)}{V_1^4},
\]
and so on.

Similarly,
\[
\lambda(s):=\frac{\Delta_7(s)}{v_5(s)}
\]
is an odd series
\[
\lambda(s)=L_1s+L_3s^3+L_5s^5+\cdots
\]
with
\[
L_1=\frac{D_2}{V_1},
\]
\[
L_3=\frac{D_4V_1-D_2V_3}{V_1^2},
\]
\[
L_5=\frac{D_6V_1^2-D_4V_1V_3+D_2(V_3^2-V_1V_5)}{V_1^3}.
\]

So, whenever \(x\) is used as the induced odd collision-side coordinate, parity
in \(s\) transfers to parity in \(x\), and one obtains
\[
Y(x)=\frac{u_5}{c}(x)\ \text{odd},
\qquad
\lambda(x)=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5}(x)\ \text{odd},
\qquad
S(x)=\frac{\lambda}{c}(x)\ \text{odd}.
\]
Consequently,
\[
Y''(x)\ \text{odd},\qquad
S''(x)\ \text{odd},
\]
hence
\[
\mathcal Z(x)=\frac{Y''}{S''}\ \text{even},
\qquad
\mathcal R(x)=\mathcal Z'(x)\ \text{odd},
\qquad
K_v=(x')^3S''\ \text{odd}.
\]
This is the parity package underlying the provisional mixed-branch exclusion
discussed below.

This is worth adding because it preserves the actual coefficient bridge you later used.

ok, can you now summarize your attack angle, and what the other chat is working on?

My attack angle is now very focused.

On the 44-point branch, I’m treating the mixed and nonmixed sides separately.

For the mixed side, I’ve been pushing the centered symmetric-placement analysis. In the centered separation variable ss, the current formulas give
u5, v5, u7,K1, v7,K1 odd in s,Δ7 even in s,
u5​, v5​, u7,K1​​, v7,K1​​ odd in s,Δ7​ even in s,

with explicit coefficients Uj,Vj,U^j,V^j,D2,D4,D6Uj​,Vj​,U
j​,V
j​,D2​,D4​,D6​. The live question there is whether this parity transfers cleanly through
x=v5c
x=cv5​​

to the good-patch coordinate. If it does, then in the xx-chart we get
Y,S odd,Z=Y′′S′′ even,R=Z′ odd,Kv odd,
Y,S odd,Z=S′′Y′′​ even,R=Z′ odd,Kv​ odd,

which would kill the whole explicit low-order mixed bad list
(r,\ord0Z)∈{(1,1),(1,3),(2,2)}.
(r,\ord0​Z)∈{(1,1),(1,3),(2,2)}.

So my current attack is: make that centered-to-patch transfer airtight and turn the mixed low-order exclusion into a theorem.

For the nonmixed side, I’ve concluded that the old centered-ss parity is probably not the right mechanism. The nonmixed branch is best expressed through
Z=Y′′S′′=Ju5Jλ,R=Z′=TvKv2,
Z=S′′Y′′​=Jλ​Ju5​​​,R=Z′=Kv2​Tv​​,

and the dangerous nonmixed low-order cases are exactly
\ord0R∈{1,3,5}.
\ord0​R∈{1,3,5}.

At the current lifted / Wronskian-ratio level, that branch is too flexible: no identity involving only c,v5,u5,Δ7c,v5​,u5​,Δ7​ and their derivatives can kill it. So the nonmixed live route is now a search for a deeper RH-specific source- or matrix-level identity that forces extra parity or vanishing of RR.

The other chat, as I understand it, is working on the complementary deeper route: hunting for the missing source-level or matrix-level structure. Concretely, that has meant three related threads:

    the source-level 22-pair factorization theorem
    I2=a1a2(h1−h2)2J2,
    I2​=a1​a2​(h1​−h2​)2J2​,

    which would close the 22-point branch once formalized;

    the source-level / involutive route on the 44-point branch, trying to see whether a corrected odd-germ symmetry descends to a reflected local coordinate and forces a parity statement on the fixed-sector scalars;

    and the matrix-level hunt around the fixed-sector packages A5f,A7fA5f​,A7f​, especially whether there is some total septic structural identity that would control
    λ=Δ7v5orJu5Jλ.
    λ=v5​Δ7​​orJλ​Ju5​​​.

So, in one line:

    I’m pushing the mixed 44-point branch through the centered-ss Taylor/parity bridge to x=v5/cx=v5​/c.

    The other chat is pushing the deeper source-/matrix-level route needed for the nonmixed 44-point branch, and also the source-level structural theorem that would finish 22-pair.
